Local News

Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association Submits to the Central Political Council, etc., Listing Various Difficulties with the Publication Law, Requesting Submission to the Legislative Yuan for Reconsideration

Since the Publication Law was promulgated in the 19th year of the Republic of China, it has been in effect for several years. Recently, the Legislative Yuan passed an amended Publication Law, which is seen as more restrictive than before. Industry colleagues in various regions have conducted in-depth research and believe that there are too many difficulties. Without reconsideration and postponement of its implementation, they have sent telegrams to the Central Political Council and the National Government, requesting reconsideration. Various Beijing-based reporters also jointly petitioned the Central Political Council, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association has prepared a detailed list of difficulties and submitted it to the Central Political Council, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Interior. The original submission is excerpted below: "Submitting this document regarding the significant impact of the Publication Law. The full text recently passed by the Legislative Yuan is even more restrictive and difficult to implement. It should be submitted for reconsideration based on different principles. It is our humble opinion that culture is the foundation of a nation, and fostering public intelligence depends on public opinion. Since the establishment of the National Government, it has adopted a policy of encouraging the news industry, tracing back to the political program established by the First National Congress of the Kuomintang, which stipulated in Article 6 of the domestic policy that the people have complete freedom of assembly, association, speech, publication, and residence. The Provisional Constitution during the Period of Political Tutelage also explicitly states freedom of speech and publication. Furthermore, the National Assembly has passed a resolution to effectively assist the news industry. Items such as postal fees and newspapers have also been subject to tax and fee reductions by the responsible ministries and departments to demonstrate promotion. It is evident that the government's support for the news industry has been comprehensive. Although the Publication Law promulgated in the 19th year cannot be considered perfect, it has provided a basis for compliance. Those engaged in the news industry have diligently followed it for years, fulfilling the state's intention to cherish and promote public opinion. However, the Legislative Yuan, acting on the instructions of your council, has re-deliberated the Publication Law and made numerous amendments, which were passed on the 12th of this month. After careful reading and consideration, our association believes that the stipulated articles differ significantly from the current law and impose even more restrictions, making implementation difficult. We hereby list the specific points below: 1. The Publication Law aims to regulate the entire publishing industry nationwide. However, an examination of all 49 articles reveals that they are almost exclusively aimed at suppressing the news industry. The issuance of newspapers requires prior registration, changes require temporary registration, and there are strict restrictions on publishers and editors, even to the point that imprisonment for more than one month would disqualify them from working in the newspaper industry again. Furthermore, various penalties are established, with punishments being severe. While this is inherent in the current law, it does not align with the goals of promoting culture, developing public intelligence, and supporting the news industry. Now that the country is gradually becoming sound and the governance is increasingly consolidated, the situation is no longer comparable to that of the 19th year. However, the new law further increases the scrutiny of organizational structure, funding sources, and distribution plans, which is even more harsh than before. Its implementation may not be helpful, as unscrupulous individuals may use deceptive language to evade suppression, while those who are cautious and conscientious may find themselves trapped. Therefore, we earnestly request your council to re-establish principles and submit them to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration, relaxing the regulations so that both urban and remote areas can establish local newspapers to assist in improving politics and guiding education. This is the first point, regarding the restrictions on the establishment of new newspapers under the Publication Law, for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration." 2. The local competent authorities for publications were previously designated as the provincial government or the municipal government under the Executive Yuan in the old law. The new law changes this to the county government and the social affairs bureau of the municipal government under the Executive Yuan, granting them more power to seize and correct publications. Newspapers are circulated nationwide, and public opinion arises from clear deliberation. Even if there are occasional lapses in judgment, senior officials should be responsible for rectifying them. However, the new law allows local county governments, etc., to take emergency measures at any time, regardless of their personnel and organization or their ability to handle the situation appropriately. If there are cases of suspicion, bias, or abuse of power, improper measures may be unavoidable. Recent incidents in various counties demonstrate the significant impact of changing the competent authorities. This is the second point for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. 3. Social news is related to public morals and should be given attention, which is of course appropriate. However, both the old and new laws already have provisions against harming good customs, and the criminal law also has specific articles on crimes such as defamation. The new law further establishes explicit provisions against publishing personal or family privacy. The distinction between public and private affairs in the news industry is often subtle, and they are often intertwined. In these degenerate times, when public morals are declining, licentiousness and transgressions directly affect the individual's privacy and indirectly affect the entire society. Praising the good and condemning the bad may slightly improve the social atmosphere. As for harming good customs and recording obscene language, there are already laws to suppress them. However, the provision on personal privacy should not be used to encompass everything, as it lacks scope and standards. If the new law is promulgated, any person being reported on, as well as the competent authorities related to the person being reported on, may use Article 38 to punish the newspaper at any time, making the news industry a target of public criticism. This may not be the intention of the legislature. Furthermore, in remote areas, competent authorities often use personal relationships to apply the articles, abuse their powers, and suppress newspapers. In such cases, they will stop at nothing. Information obtained by public security organs may become a problem in society but may not involve litigation in the judiciary. Such cases are common. In the future, once published, there will be even more disputes, which will undoubtedly harm the development of the news industry. This is the third point for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. 4. Advertisements and announcements are the responsibility of the person who publishes them. Newspapers usually carefully select the manuscripts they receive and would never deliberately violate the regulations to invite trouble. However, private advertisements and announcements made by lawyers on behalf of their clients often involve personal or family privacy. How can newspapers alone be held responsible for such private legal actions? The news industry has a significant impact on the safety and security of the entire nation and the rise and fall of the nation, so the penalties are also the most severe in Article 19, Section 4. Even in the most extreme cases, the imprisonment is only two years, and the fine is only less than one thousand yuan. However, newspapers that indirectly publish private legal actions may be punished according to Article 38, with six months of imprisonment and a fine of five hundred yuan. The disparity in severity is not fair. This is the fourth point for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. 5. Article 22 of the new law adds the words "politics and local security" to the items to be considered during wartime or in times of turmoil, compared to the current law. During wartime and times of turmoil, unity of purpose and concerted efforts are the disciplines that citizens should abide by, without the need for unnecessary words. However, the political aspect is already comprehensively covered by the provisions of Article 19, Section 4. Local security often occurs suddenly, and the scope varies greatly. If it is necessary to rely on the orders of the National Government, it will be too late to take emergency measures. The local competent authorities, such as the county government, may also exaggerate or conceal the facts by citing the articles. If there are no restrictions at all, it is not a safe plan, but a broad statement is difficult to follow. This is the fifth point for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. 6. When a newspaper publishes something and someone requests a correction, it is customary to publish the correction. This is not only a business practice but also a moral obligation. The current law specifies a special article stating that the correction should be given a position equivalent to the original article. The new law changes this to the same position. A single word makes a big difference. Placing it in the same position is often factually difficult. For example, if the first section is disclosed today, and a correction is made tomorrow, the timeliness will be lost, and it will never be placed in the first column again. Although this is a trivial matter, there is absolutely no problem according to custom. It is unnecessary to list it in the article. Furthermore, disputes between the two parties are numerous, and each party makes corrections. Lengthy articles are published, and each party insists on its own opinion. Newspapers find it difficult to investigate and verify within three days, especially from distant places. If they are published as they are, there will be no distinction between right and wrong. Newspapers will face difficulties that cannot be expressed. This is the sixth point for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. 7. The responsibilities of publishers, authors, etc., are not clearly defined in this law. Articles 37, 38, and 39 list publishers, editors, authors, and printers together, without explaining whether they are jointly punished. Article 40 states that those who are responsible for the publication and signing of the articles are to be punished according to Article 37, and the same applies to those who are punished according to Article 39. The meaning of the legislation is not clear, and the articles are difficult to find. Editors may take short vacations, and temporary replacements may be negligent. If the person at fault has no responsibility, while the person on vacation is punished, it is unfair. The news published in daily newspapers comes from various sources and is not usually signed. However, it is now said that those who sign the article are responsible for the punishment, leaving newspapers at a loss. This is the seventh point for which we respectfully request your council to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. Furthermore, this law only contains articles on government suppression, with no opportunities for newspapers to appeal. If the law is promulgated and implemented, and the relevant authorities take inappropriate measures or make mistakes in seizure and punishment, newspapers will be banned, and public opinion will be suppressed. What legal remedies can be taken in administrative procedures? Newspapers value circulation, and rapid distribution is especially important. Even if an appeal is successful afterward, the time for postal delivery has passed, and the timeliness of the newspaper is completely lost. How will this loss be compensated? The spirit of national legislation and the government's intention to support the news industry should not be like this. In summary, we respectfully submit this document to your council, requesting that you thoroughly investigate it from both a legal and factual perspective, so as to avoid difficulties in implementation after promulgation. Your council is the highest political body in the country and will surely understand the root causes and consider the established rules. We respectfully request that you re-establish principles and submit them for reconsideration, so that the law can be fully implemented and freedom of speech can be effectively protected. We urgently present our words and are deeply grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Political Conference of the Central Executive Committee." (Rest omitted)

National Foreign Trade: Import Surplus in the First Half of the Year Exceeded 286,085,622 Yuan

According to the Shenshi News Agency, the Customs announced yesterday the status of our national foreign trade for the first half of the year, from January to June. The total import value was 545,552,950 yuan in national currency, a decrease of 24,394,541 yuan compared to 569,849,836 yuan in the same period last year. The total export value was 259,369,673 yuan in national currency, a decrease of 9,175,041 yuan compared to 268,544,714 yuan in the same period last year. The import surplus was 286,085,622 yuan.

Increased Import Surplus in June

In June alone, the value of foreign trade imports reached 91,526,641 yuan in national currency, an increase of 5,267,228 yuan compared to the same period last year and a decrease of 4,605,200 yuan compared to May. The value of exports reached 41,229,246 yuan in national currency, a decrease of 7,943,550 yuan compared to the same period last year and an increase of 447,251 yuan compared to May. The import surplus reached 50,297,395 yuan, a significant increase compared to the import surplus of 37,086,617 yuan in the same period last year.

Sharp Increase in Tung Oil Exports

Among the main native products exported overseas in the first half of the year, tung oil exports were particularly active, reaching a value of 18,938,081 yuan, an increase of one-third compared to the export value of over 12 million yuan in the same period last year, ranking first among export goods this year. Exports of raw and tanned hides and leather goods reached 15,148,558 yuan, eggs and egg products 13,814,581 yuan, peanuts 11,800,321 yuan, tea 12,069,149 yuan, sesame 10,015,766 yuan, cotton 4,437,877 yuan, and pig bristles 6,403,862 yuan (all in national currency).

Imported Rice Ranks First

Among the main foreign goods imported in the first half of the year, rice ranked first with a value of 43,359,190 customs gold units, equivalent to over 75 million yuan in national currency, accounting for 14% of the total value of foreign goods imported in the first half of the year. Other imports included cotton 16,846,542 yuan, metals and ores 29,376,711 yuan, machinery and tools 16,742,743 yuan, wheat 16,783,029 yuan, sugar 10,011,771 yuan, and kerosene 21,884,626 yuan (all in customs gold units).

Kong Xiangxi and Ye Chucang left Beijing on the overnight express train yesterday and arrived in Shanghai this morning.

Xu Fu Talks About Visiting Kong to Discuss Finance, Construction Bonds, and Mortgaging Existing Funds; Preliminary Contact Has Been Made with the Banking Community

Xu Fu, the Director of Finance of the Fujian Provincial Government, recently came to Shanghai from Fujian to visit Minister Kong to discuss the financial problems of Fujian Province and the mortgaging of existing funds for local construction bonds. Xu met with reporters from the Central News Agency at the City Bank yesterday morning. According to him, after the suppression of bandits in Fujian Province, construction needs to be undertaken, requiring a large amount of funds. This trip to Shanghai is to report on provincial affairs to Chairman Chen, who is staying in Shanghai, and to meet with Minister Kong, who is coming to Shanghai, to discuss financial issues. Regarding the local construction bond of 3 million yuan, after the approval of the Executive and Legislative Yuans, a portion of the bond, approximately 1 million yuan, has been mortgaged to the banking community in Fujian Province and handed over to the Construction Department for use. The remaining 2 million yuan of face value will be negotiated with the banking community in Shanghai for mortgage. He met with bankers on the 24th for initial contact, but a decision can only be made after discussing it with Minister Kong. The mortgage banking group will be chaired by the Central Bank. Xu continued, stating that the affairs of the province are currently busy and need to be dealt with urgently. Therefore, if Minister Kong can come to Shanghai this morning to meet and discuss, he will take a boat back to Fujian that night.

A Section of Track Near the South Station Will Be Temporarily Disconnected This Morning; French Water Company Agreed with the Railway Bureau to Bury Water Pipes Across the Track

The section of track at the Shanghai South Station West Gate of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway was dismantled at 4:30 this morning, cutting off traffic, until 7:00, when traffic was restored. The French-owned Lujiawan Water Company plans to bury a water pipe under the railway track at that location. The company's engineers contacted Engineer Luo of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway and reached an agreement to allow the work to begin at 4:30 this morning and be completed by approximately 7:00. Fortunately, no passenger or freight trains passed through that road during this time. Yesterday, the Engineering Department notified all stations accordingly.

Mingxing and Jiangda, Two Vessels Rescue Stranded Ships

The Sanbei Company's Mingxing ship ran aground on the right bank of Yangluo, 60 miles downstream of Hankou. After three failed attempts to tow it, all 3,000 officers and soldiers and hundreds of horses on board were transferred. The heavy objects inside the ship were unloaded. Two large towing barges were used to tow it. Fortunately, although the downstream water level was decreasing, it was the peak season for upstream water levels. The ship was successfully towed off the ground on Wednesday afternoon and is now heading to Hankou. According to the shipowner's report, the stranding was due to the Jianghan Customs having moved the Yangluo lightship after the flood to prevent accidents. However, the Mingxing ship was in Nanjing at the time and was unaware of this, resulting in the accidental grounding. The company has telegraphed all ships to inform them to avoid further accidents. The China Merchants Bureau's Jiangda ship ran aground on the opposite bank of Yangluo on the night of the 19th. Jiangyu and Meicheng were sent to tow it, but they were unable to pull it off the sandbar. Later, the shipowner, Feng Jun, personally went to Hankou and rented two large towing barges from Taikoo, which towed it off the ground after five hours. Only the car leaves were slightly detached. After being tied up, it was able to sail to Hankou. This happened on Tuesday night. Yesterday's telegram stated that it had safely escaped.

Page 10

Yangtze River Water Levels Fall, Shipping Gradually Resumes; Four Chartered Vessels Departed Yesterday

Flooding Halts Cargo

During the major flooding of the Yangtze River, Hankou was in grave danger. The bottom floors of the wharves and warehouses of various shipping companies could not hold cargo. The wharf laborers were requisitioned for flood control, causing almost all cargo transportation to be halted. The business of all ships was affected.

River Water Recedes

In the past few days, the weather in Hankou has been very good, and the river water has receded significantly. Local shipping companies received telegrams from the Hankou branch yesterday, stating that the water level in Hankou had dropped two feet in the past two days (23rd and 24th), and the danger has passed. People's hearts are at ease, and the water has also receded along the coast, allowing for the resumption of loading and unloading operations at all wharves. The Shanghai branch has been requested to immediately resume shipping goods to Hankou. Various shipping companies have followed suit. Starting today, there will be no restrictions on the loading of goods bound for Hankou.

Anhui Also Reopens

Wuhu initially requested the suspension of shipments from Shanghai due to the inability of the wharves to accommodate cargo. Anqing followed suit. The suspension of shipments to Anhui by various ships in Shanghai has lasted for more than ten days. Yesterday, a telegram was suddenly received from Anqing, reporting that the water in Anhui has gradually receded, and the wharves can handle the loading and unloading of passengers and cargo. Please resume normal loading of goods from Shanghai. It is reported that various companies have resumed shipping.

Chartered Cargo

The Yangtze River charter has been implemented since yesterday. The first batch of goods being shipped to the Yangtze River, calculated by charter, included the Jiang of the China Merchants Bureau, the Ningjing of the Ningshao Company, the Wuchang of the Taizan Company, and the Ruihe of Jardine Matheson. The calculation for cargo leaving Hankou will also begin with the ships departing yesterday.

Qingning Has Arrived in Keelung; Zhuang Huibo Says It Will Arrive in Shanghai on the 29th

The Hwaning Shipping Company's Qingning ship, with a deadweight of 1,951 tons, usually travels along the northern and southern coasts. The ship transported goods from Shanghai to Shantou, unloaded all the cargo, and then went to Keelung to load coal to return to Shanghai. However, when it reached the South China Sea, it encountered a hurricane. In the past three days, the ship had not telegraphed Shanghai to notify its itinerary, leading to rumors in Shanghai that the whereabouts of the Qingning ship were unknown, and its whereabouts were unknown for a time, arousing the deep attention of the shipping industry in Shanghai. The insurance industry was particularly concerned. This reporter went to the Hwaning Company on Sijing Road to inquire. According to the manager of the company, Zhuang Huibo, the Qingning has arrived in Keelung today (referring to the 25th) and is now loading coal. It has not been lost. After loading coal in Keelung, it will sail to Shanghai and is expected to arrive on the 29th.

Bank Association Amends Constitution; Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Approves for Record

The Shanghai Bank Association amended Article 3 of its constitution, regarding the procedures for member banks to join the association. The fourth general meeting of members had previously approved the principles and handed them over to the Executive Committee to formulate the amended articles, which were submitted to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for record. The association has now received an order from the Social Affairs Bureau approving it for record. After receiving the orders from the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, they will be forwarded to the members for compliance, so that banks that want to join the association in the future can follow the amended procedures.

Mr. Yang Yinpu's Opinion: Bank Acceptance Drafts – More Advantages than Disadvantages, a Major Advancement for Our Financial Organization, Greatly Aiding the Development of Industry and Commerce

The Central China Times reports that the banking sector is planning to create bank acceptance drafts to expand credit and aid industry and commerce. All sectors have unanimously expressed their approval, and the implementation is only a matter of time. It is reported that the acceptance drafts were originally scheduled to be implemented on August 1st, but it is feared that it will be too late. It is rumored that the implementation date will be changed to around August 10th, so that the industrial and commercial sectors can issue acceptance drafts during the August festival this year and obtain financial circulation. The Central China Times reporter interviewed economist Mr. Yang Yinpu yesterday. According to him, since the financial crisis in Shanghai, which resulted in a credit crunch, the general use of funds has become constrained. Due to the low social credit, financial institutions find it difficult to issue loans, leading to stagnant capital. Industrial and commercial enterprises, on the other hand, are suffering from the inability to use funds, resulting in a decline in the overall market. Recently, people in the banking sector, recognizing this, have started bank acceptance drafts to expand the use of bills. This matter is very beneficial to improving the current financial situation. Without this bank acceptance draft, the credit aspect has the double guarantee of actual goods and the banking sector's funds. Its reliability is above bank drafts and commercial acceptance drafts. Its impact on social finance is also more advantageous than disadvantageous, and the scope of circulation and use in the market in the future can be infinitely expanded. For example, at the beginning of the establishment, the fund amount is set at 50 million yuan. In the future, if the society is stable and the general production volume increases, the total amount of acceptance drafts can also be increased accordingly. The flexibility is very convenient. At the same time, after the circulation of this type of bill in the future, not only will the industrial and commercial sectors benefit, but also individual investment will have new outlets. The indirect effects will have a great effect on the development of production enterprises. Moreover, if bank acceptance drafts are widely circulated, a clearing system can be created invisibly in the future. Banks can collect payments without mortgages and focus on discount business. Finally, according to Mr. Yang, the previous commercial acceptance drafts of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce were intended to replace credit loans, and the purpose of the current creation of bank acceptance drafts is also to replace mortgage loans. China's financial organization and structure have made such reasonable progress due to encountering difficulties, which is indeed a good phenomenon.

Wang Qingmu's Detailed Suggestions to the Jiangsu Supervisory Commissioner: One on Local Taxes, One on Provincial Government Organization

Mr. Qingmu, a gentleman from Jiangsu Province, submitted a detailed statement to Mr. Ding Chaowu, the Jiangsu District Supervisory Commissioner, regarding local taxes and provincial government organization matters. The original text is excerpted below. Regarding the detailed statement, I believe that from ancient times to the present, the beauty of governance should be attributed to the Han Dynasty. At that time, there were governors who traveled around the prefectures and states. Gu Tinglin called it a good law that would not change for a hundred generations. The Ming Dynasty's censors, who inspected the local areas, can be said to have captured the meaning of the ancients. Now, the National Government's Control Yuan has reports from the supervisory commissioners of various provinces, and our Jiangsu has the arrival of Your Excellency to rectify the officialdom and relieve the people's difficulties. The responsibility is very heavy, and the expectations are very high. Are there any members of the public who are not rejoicing and excited? In the Book of History, one chapter says to widely consult, the second chapter says to widely deliberate, the third chapter says to widely measure, and the fourth chapter says to widely inquire, which shows the diligence in visiting and consulting, and not being afraid of trouble. Recently, as the carriage is about to depart, cases from various regions are coming one after another. Given the vastness of Jiangsu Province and the large population, if every matter, no matter how big or small, is properly handled, I am afraid that there will not be enough time. How should we distinguish between the important and the urgent? Which ones must be handled personally, which ones should be sent to the subordinates to investigate and report, and then submitted for review and approval? Which ones should be transferred to the judiciary for fair judgment? Other trivial and non-urgent matters should be put aside. Then, focus your attention and investigation on officials who are corrupt and shield local bullies. Expose the evidence of their entanglement and expand the fields. For the people who are suffering and feel trapped, and whose livelihood is on the verge of collapse, rescue them as soon as possible. Clean up the discipline of the country, relieve the people from their plight. The news spreads, and the public listens attentively. It is like a great drought receiving timely rain, turning barren areas into fertile land. It all depends on the current actions of Your Excellency. Is the public's expectation not important? Qingmu has personally witnessed the special difficulties, forgetting his old age. He has been studying the gains and losses of politics and believes that there are things that urgently need to be corrected and reformed. I would like to sincerely tell Your Excellency about one thing: the improper distribution of local taxes. Land tax has always been a major source of national revenue, so local expenses are also paid from the land tax. Since the separation of national and local taxes, land tax has been used exclusively for local taxes. According to the interpretation of the word "local," it should be based on the county as the main body, not the province. Now, looking at the budget prepared by our Jiangsu Province, all the land tax revenue is used as provincial tax, and the county does not receive any of it. The additional tax of two and a half cents per tael of silver, which was previously collected, has now been changed to a special fund for provincial education, which is no different from the regular tax. The additional tax of three cents per tael of silver, which was previously collected, and the county additional tax of one yuan per stone in the canal counties, is now called county regular tax. The total amount for the entire province is only two to three million yuan. Therefore, the county's local autonomy projects all rely on additional taxes for support. The mu tax is the larger of the additional taxes. If it is not enough, they take it from harsh and miscellaneous taxes. At this time of commercial depression, the people are haggard, and the countryside is bankrupt. It is difficult to scrape together. The central government, in view of this, has established a local donation and tax supervision committee to sort out, select, and reduce or exempt the harsh ones. The intention is very sincere, but there are too many constraints. It is already extremely difficult to cut one to two million yuan from the entire province, let alone more? Even if one to two million yuan can be cut, it will still not save the people from poverty, let alone if it cannot be cut? Article 3 of the Executive Yuan's Measures for Reorganizing Land Tax Surcharges last year stipulates that the total amount of surcharges shall not exceed the regular tax. Furthermore, Article 2 of the Ministry of Finance's Measures for Restricting Land Tax Surcharges stipulates that counties with land tax surcharges exceeding the regular tax shall find ways to reduce them to at most the same amount as the regular tax. It can be seen that the Executive Yuan and the Ministry deeply know that the people cannot bear the burden, so there are these regulations for reducing taxes. The people were overjoyed when they heard about it, thinking that there was hope for recovery. But who knew that the provincial government could not implement it? The county's autonomous expenses all rely on additional taxes, and the trend is that they will only increase without end. How can taxes be reduced? As the saying goes, if the people are sufficient, with whom will the ruler be insufficient? If the people are insufficient, with what will the ruler be sufficient? It is also said that having a heart that cannot bear to see people suffer is having a government that cannot bear to see people suffer. The worthies in the Jiangsu Provincial Government, coming from the fields, have often seen the people's insufficiency, and must have a heart that cannot bear to see them suffer. For the current plan, the county is the main body of local autonomy. The Legislative Yuan has already resolved that land tax should belong to the county. We should advance the plan to provide land tax to cover county expenses, as well as deed tax and various business taxes. As for land tax surcharges, follow the orders of the Executive Yuan and the Ministry, and temporarily allow collection up to the amount of the regular tax. In this way, local autonomy will have a legitimate source of tax revenue, the people's strength will be slightly relieved, and the arrears of taxes will be less. This is the saying that the distribution of local taxes should be changed. The organization of the provincial government is not good. The province is the name of a government office, which first appeared in the Wei and Jin Dynasties. It was the Central Secretariat. In the Yuan Dynasty, the Central Secretariat's Provincial Branch was established, intending to centralize power. The Ming and Qing dynasties followed this, but the name of the province was inherited, and the original meaning was lost. By the Republic of China, there were provinces that did not obey the orders of the central government, which was equivalent to the Tang Dynasty's feudal towns. Since the National Government moved to Nanjing, the provincial government has a committee system, with one person serving as chairman and various departments set up, with committee members concurrently serving as heads. There are also several committee members who do not concurrently serve as heads. All politics are decided by meetings. Although the name is public, there are many constraints. The expenses are huge, and the effectiveness is weak. Recently, several provinces have changed to joint offices, probably because the department system is not suitable for provincial administration. Fifty years ago, Wu Zhihui proposed to shrink the province area, aiming for quick implementation of policies. However, shrinking the province area and still using the current committee system is absolutely impossible. It is better to abolish the name of the province and call it a prefecture. Taking Jiangsu as an example, apart from the two cities of Nanjing and Shanghai, the area south of the Yangtze River is divided into two prefectures, and the area north of the Yangtze River is divided into four prefectures, which are directly under the central government and under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Interior. The head of the prefecture is called the prefect, and the name implies that he is actually guarding the land. The expenses of the prefecture are provided by the counties under its jurisdiction. Each prefecture and county has a council, and members are selected from local impartial gentry. The country establishes officials, divided into two levels, the ministries and commissions and the prefectures and counties. The central government controls from a high position, just like the body uses the arms, and the arms use the fingers. If the bones and joints are difficult to communicate, there will be no danger of the tail wagging the dog. Compared to the current equality of ministries and provinces, where the ministry's orders cannot be implemented in the provinces, the benefits cannot be enumerated. The country takes the people as its foundation, and local autonomy takes the county as the unit. How the people's strength goes from weak to strong, and how the county changes, all depend on the surplus or deficit of expenses as the key to progress or retreat. The Canal tax is renamed land tax, and the full amount belongs to the county. Large counties are certainly affluent, but small counties have less revenue, so they can be merged as appropriate to equalize them. Now, Jiangning is indeed a rich county with hope for development. Zhenjiang and Donghai counties are considered poor by the provincial government and are trying to help them. I don't know that the national crisis is becoming more urgent, and the people's livelihood is becoming more difficult. The responsibility of saving the country and seeking survival should be borne by the people of the whole country together. The development of local projects should strive for equality, but it is not possible to make a trial in a certain county and make other counties feel neglected. It is known that the expenses of a certain county are insufficient and it is being helped. Where are those whose expenses are not insufficient? It is only possible to help a certain number of counties and make other counties feel partiality. It is only when the Ding Cao tax items belong to the county, and the power of the high prefectures and counties is jointly held, that those who have been concentrated in the cities and have no place to live can all be sent back to their hometowns. The various bureaus of the mountains, prefectures, and counties can use their talents and abilities to do what they can. Only then can the politics be clear and the local development will naturally be achieved accordingly. This is the saying that the provincial government's official system should be changed and reorganized. The above two points are all about reform. Whether the reasons are sufficient or not, I will not seek to be detailed in my arguments. I sincerely hope that Your Excellency will pay attention to the investigation at any time and in any place. In a month or two, if what I said is not wrong, please report to the Control Yuan and submit it to the court. Moreover, Qingmu has more to say. The regular land tax of Jiangsu Province is more than 11 million yuan. The additional taxes are collected in accordance with the orders of the Executive Yuan and the Ministry, also totaling more than 11 million yuan. Now that the land is being surveyed and the accumulation is being organized, the regular tax will increase, and the additional tax can be reduced even more. The deed tax of the entire province is more than one million yuan. If it is changed to belong to the county, the income will definitely increase. The business tax of the entire province is more than 4 million taels, and it costs a lot to send personnel to collect it. There are even more malpractices in bidding and contracting. If it is changed to belong to the county, the method should avoid harming the people, and the collection will also be more accurate. All of these sayings are taken from the local and used in the local. If the civil administration is carried out in an orderly manner, the national strength will naturally increase invisibly. If it is like the current county, it is like a bird's foot. The virtuous county magistrate is trapped by the economy, bound by laws, and restricted, and there is nothing that can be done. Those who are unworthy are good at perfunctory, accustomed to deception, cruelly oppressing the people, and only seeking to benefit themselves. The provincial government is too high, and the people's hidden feelings are ultimately separated. The examination of the subordinates is also sparse. Only by changing to a two-level system of prefectures and counties can the civil administration atmosphere be refreshed. Therefore, the reform of the two matters must be considered consistently to achieve success. Qingmu's foolishness does not dare to be presumptuous. A thousand thoughts may lead to one success. Silence is difficult to bear. The deep concern for the times and the ardent love for the country make me unaware of the taboos. I only ask for understanding and forgiveness.

New Early Rice from Pudong Enters the Market

The new early rice from Pudong in the South City entered the market yesterday. The goods were transported from Yitai Rice Shop in Zhoupu Bridge to Shanghai, totaling thirteen stones of rough rice. It was entrusted to Xinchang Rice Mill in Xuejiabang to be milled and sold. The mill produced eleven stones and five dou of white rice. The rice quality is exceptionally clean, and the grain color is particularly smooth. It is indeed a fresh and good product. Moreover, this is the first batch to enter the market this year, so the market price is also brisk, with a selling price of eleven yuan per stone. It is said that Pudong has had a bumper harvest this year, and the weather has been relatively smooth, resulting in a yield of 60-70%.

Typhoon Warning: Ning Uses Wired Radio; Ministry of Industry Order Instructs Fishery Protection Agencies to be Informed

The Ministry of Industry issued an order to the Ministry of Industry's Fishery Protection Office yesterday: "Regarding the matter of sending typhoon telegrams to various fishing areas, the Ministry of Transportation previously approved a consultation stating that it would be implemented from July 1st. Typhoon warnings will be broadcast by the Central Meteorological Research Institute. Agencies in various fishing areas can install radios to listen to the broadcasts. It is not necessary for the telegraph office to forward telegrams, etc. This has been consulted with the governments of coastal provinces and forwarded for notification. Now, a letter from the Shanghai Xujiahui Observatory states: 'Regarding the installation of radio receivers in various fishing grounds, it is indeed an important plan. However, according to my 15 years of experience, it seems that it is better to still use telegrams. The reason is that the warnings issued by the city to the various fishing grounds, if transmitted by shortwave radio, cannot be considered to have reached the fishing grounds without a response. Recently, radio waves are often congested, and messages are often delayed and need to be resent. When issuing warnings, several lines must be sent simultaneously. If there is an error, the danger is extremely serious. Therefore, it is better to forward the telegrams, which is more reliable. If the location of the fishing ground does not have a telegraph office, it may be possible to install a radio receiver and a repeater to request a resend if the message cannot reach. At the same time, I propose that your office order all steamship fishing boats and fishery protection vessels to pay attention to the warnings issued by Shanghai.' This is hereby approved. Regarding the installation of a repeater and paying attention to the warnings issued by Shanghai, the above is still proper and can be used as a reference for installing radio receivers to listen to typhoon telegrams. You are hereby ordered to be informed. This order."

Appeals for Flood Relief from Various Provinces

Xu Jingren, Chairman of the National Government Relief Committee and Vice-Chairman of the Relief Committee for Drought Disasters in Various Provinces, telegraphed Hu Guigeng, the manager of Yong An Tang in Shanghai, and Lang Jingshan yesterday, requesting them to relay a message to the Hu Wenhu and Hu Wenbao brothers in Singapore, asking for donations of medicines such as Wan Jin You (Tiger Balm), Bagua Dan (Eight Trigram Pills), and Qing Huo Shui (Heat-Clearing Water) to help the disaster-stricken people. The original telegram is recorded as follows: "To Mr. Hu Guigeng, Manager of Yong An Tang in Shanghai, and Mr. Lang Jingshan, please quickly forward this to Mr. Hu Wenhu and Mr. Hu Wenbao for their kind attention. This year, the Yangtze River has flooded, and looking at the upstream counties of Tianmen and Hanchuan, all who have visited sigh at the submersion. Today, I turned to Hunan, inquiring and learning that the disaster situation is also severe. The disaster victims have been living in the water for a long time, and diseases are taking lives. It is said that after a flood, there must be a great epidemic. Considering this, I cannot rest easy. I have long admired your deep concern, and your pharmacy's medicines are particularly effective. I respectfully request a generous donation and prompt dispatch to facilitate distribution and save lives. This is a special telegram, asking for your benevolent consideration. Respectfully, Xu Shiying." Mr. Hu received the telegram and has already forwarded it to Singapore, it is said.

This time, the dikes of the Yellow River and the Yangtze River collapsed simultaneously, and the disaster situation is extraordinarily severe. The General and Branch Associations of the Red Swastika Society have jointly organized relief teams to set off in different directions. The first team, led by Han Yongxiang, set off for counties such as Juancheng in Shandong Province to implement relief efforts. The second team, led by Yan Chenglong, set off for the Changyuan area to investigate and distribute emergency relief. The Nanjing Southeast Main Association organized a third team, and Wu Heguang, the general captain, gathered team members and sent Ouyang Dulin to lead the team, carrying a large quantity of medicines to set off for various disaster areas in Hubei. When the Yellow River breached its banks, the branch associations in Shandong Province, such as the Jinan and Jining associations, immediately organized relief teams to set off in different directions to provide dry food and set up shelters to accommodate refugees from various places. The local Shanghai Red Swastika Society is actively raising funds. However, the disaster is extremely severe, and the affected area is vast. It is hoped that all sectors will rise up and work together to provide relief.

The Hubei Association in Shanghai received a joint telegram from various legal entities in Tianmen and 800,000 people in the county, saying (titles omitted) all esteemed sirs: It is said that Tianmen has been known as a "water country" since ancient times, with a low-lying terrain and a dense population of over 800,000. In recent years, disasters have occurred frequently, and the people have not recovered from their difficulties. Unfortunately, this year in June, heavy rain fell for ten consecutive days, and all the county's cultivated land was flooded. In addition, on July 8th, eleven sections of the Xiang embankment belonging to Zhong were breached, pouring down with the force of a high-pitched roof. Although the military and civilians tried their best to build repairs, the water level was more than ten feet higher than the surface of the dikes in various places. Within a few days, they collapsed one after another. The people's houses, grain, livestock, in the county town and various towns and villages were swept away by the flood like fallen leaves in the autumn wind. Only the sound of wailing and cries for help on the water could be heard, colliding with the turbulent waves. Making hundreds of thousands of lives become fish and turtles is truly an unprecedented disaster in hundreds of years. The scene is no less than the breach at Changyuan. What is even more tragic is that the survivors who have been spared have lost their fathers and sons, and their wives and children are gone. Some are staying on the treetops, or clinging to the roofs. During the day, the scorching sun burns their skin, and at night, the cold dew pierces their bones. They drink turbid water to prolong their lives. Those who have been rescued by rescue boats or have struggled to escape and are fortunate enough to escape the danger gather on the remaining dikes, without clothes or food, crying for their children and husbands, feeling that life is worse than death. Now, the water势 has slightly decreased, but the city walls, embankments, and the few remaining houses are still in the midst of the great flood. If the water rises again in a day, there is a danger of submersion. Moreover, after the flood, plagues are easy to occur, and after hunger, bandits are easy to arise. All aspects of sanitation, medicine, post-disaster relief, and disaster relief need to be carried out urgently, and large-scale relief efforts must be made to be effective. Although various agencies and legal entities have tried their best to provide relief, they are also in the disaster area, and all their reserves have been exhausted. A drop in the bucket is of no help to the overall situation. Therefore, on behalf of all the disaster-stricken people in the county, we cry out to the national officials and elders, brothers and sisters, earnestly requesting you to extend your helping hands and jointly rescue the disaster-stricken people, gathering the strength of all to work together for good deeds, so that we can provide for the dead and care for the living. We are infinitely grateful and await your orders."

In addition, a joint telegram was received from Zhang Naiwei, Yang Fengxiang, Deng Bicheng, and all twenty-two members of the Yidu County Flood Relief Emergency Committee (titles omitted), saying: "Our county straddles the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, at the key exit of the Sichuan River. The Qingjiang, Han River, and Yang River run through its south, and the Manao River encircles its north. The mountains within the territory are scattered and extremely barren. The fertile agricultural areas are generally located in the areas bordering the river. Every time we encounter peach and summer floods, we suffer from water disasters. However, since the beginning of history, there has never been a flood as strange and severe as this year's flood. Since the morning of July 1st and until the morning of the 7th, heavy rain fell continuously for four days and nights, causing flash floods and a sudden rise in river water, surging and frightening. The water level was more than seven feet higher than that of the 20th year of the Republic of China. With the addition of rapid thunder, strong winds, and torrential rain, most of the public and private houses in the city and countryside collapsed. People, animals, utensils, bamboo, and wood were swept down the river along both banks. All the dikes were almost completely collapsed. Because the water rose too quickly, the residents could not avoid it in time, and they were tossed about in a vast expanse of water, either raising their hands to wait for help or clinging to the trees to call for help. The cries of children and the weeping of children were unbearable to see and hear. The military and political agencies immediately supervised the team doctors and took various measures to rescue them, and on the 1st and 2nd days, the county government repeatedly reported the situation by telegram. Except for the remote areas where transportation has not yet been restored, we are currently engaged in investigation. All the administrative districts under the county are among the worst affected. The most affected parts include Longwo River, Huangjia River, and Guolu Tan in the first district; Xiongdu, Niejihe, Xiyangping, and Liujin Tan in the second district; Chadian City, Honghua Tao, Gulao Bei, Shanxi Dachong, Shangxia Shawan, Zhaping, and Dujia Tuo in the third district; and Baiyang, Anfu City, Shaqi Ping, Linjia Jia, and Luojia River in the fourth district. The fields and houses were all washed away by the flood. Even the barren land on the mountains, known as highlands, where taro, silkworms, and soap seedlings are planted, were also uprooted and washed into the flood along with the soil, leaving nothing behind. Although the flooded area accounts for only two-thirds of the entire territory, the disaster-stricken locations are spread throughout the county. Currently, we have provided shelter to more than 5,000 disaster victims who have come to the city. It is still difficult to obtain accurate statistics on those whose wives and children are scattered, who have been lost or are missing, or who are fortunate enough to survive but have no food or clothing and no home to return to. With such widespread sorrow and hunger, if we do not receive a quick allocation of large sums of money to provide emergency relief, the survivors will have no hope of survival, and the local order is likely to be unimaginable. We, Naiwei, have decided to establish the Yidu County Flood Relief Emergency Committee according to the resolutions of the local agencies and legal entities to temporarily alleviate the immediate crisis and have reported it. The details will be submitted after the investigation is completed. The magnitude of this disaster is beyond the capacity of one corner. Therefore, we appeal by telegram, earnestly requesting you to find ways to provide relief to benefit the disaster-stricken people and plan for post-disaster recovery. We respectfully lead the 300,000 people of Tuyi, eagerly awaiting your orders."

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Prevents Suicide: Drawing Alerting Pictures, Depicting the Painful Conditions of Suicide, and Hanging Them in Various Districts to Alert Citizens

In recent years, the social economy has been exhausted, unemployment has increased, and the weak are in a difficult environment with no way to make a living. After being slightly stimulated, they suddenly develop a sense of world-weariness. Therefore, unfortunate suicide incidents occur almost every day. Especially in this city, where Chinese and foreigners live together and the population is dense, those who are forced to take desperate measures are countless. In view of this, the Municipal Public Security Bureau believes that suicide incidents are detrimental to the future of the country and the nation. Although the authorities pay great attention to this, such as Director Wu of the Social Affairs Bureau, who has published opinions on preventing suicide, and whose thorough discussion can be used as a warning to awaken those who are misguided, it is essential to prevent this trend from growing and to find ways to prevent it. Therefore, the authorities have specially instructed the department to draw various alerting pictures depicting the pain of suicide and make dozens of large posters to be nailed to public places on the roads, alleys, and streets in the city, as well as at wharves, riverbanks, and bridges, to warn citizens who are temporarily pessimistic and suicidal, so that they can turn back from the brink. In the future, suicide incidents may be reduced through this passive prevention.

The Police Strictly Prohibit the Abuse of Car Horns

Regarding the prohibition of noise in the city, the Acting Superintendent of the Police Department of the Public Works Department has recently devised a method to strictly prohibit the abuse of car horns when unnecessary and the excessive volume of horns. Article 30 of the Traffic Regulations of the Concession will be actively implemented to prohibit the abuse of horns and causing annoyance. The plan has now been submitted by the Acting Superintendent to the Police Committee and then to the Board of Directors for approval and will be implemented soon. The Acting Superintendent also stated that Article 40 of the Traffic Regulations is difficult to implement because the sound standard is difficult to determine. Therefore, he has investigated with the Public Works Department whether there is a machine that can determine the sound level and record it in units for reference. If there is such a machine with a suitable price and size, the sound of car horns will be uniform and will not be a problem. The following is a record of Articles 30 and 40 of the Traffic Regulations, so that drivers know what to follow: Article 30: Drivers are not allowed to use horns, bells, or other signals when unnecessary, or to use such signals in a way that causes annoyance. Article 40: Cars must be equipped with a device that can emit an audible and sufficient warning when the car is approaching. The device must be approved by the Bureau. Except for fire and police vehicles, it is not allowed to use gongs, steam horns, whistles, or alarm bells.

What Was Seen During the Day Was Jupiter

In the past two days, a star was discovered in Shanghai during the day. Many people stopped on the road to watch. At 12:00 noon, the star was right overhead. Even during the day, the starlight was still bright and radiant. According to astronomers, this star is Jupiter, one of the eight major planets. Its path is the most changeable. This star can be seen with the naked eye during the day. Usually, because its orbit is either too far south or too far north, people do not pay attention to it. Now it has moved overhead, and people can see it because it is closer. In fact, according to astronomical observations, this is a very normal thing.

A Rotten Infant Was Found in the Sewer: Confirmed to Have Been Stillborn and Abandoned by Someone Unknown

At around 4:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, three or five naughty children were playing the game of rolling copper coins in front of No. 307, south of the French Tibetan Temple on Grole Road in the French Concession. One of the children's copper coins rolled into the sewer hole on the east side of the road. The child then opened the sewer cover to retrieve the fallen copper coin, reaching down and pushing aside the floating dirt. A strange and foul smell immediately hit his nose. Upon closer inspection, it was the corpse of a female child who had been dead for many days. The body had already rotted, and the children were frightened and ran away after discovering it. The residents of the area reported it to the police station, which sent detectives to investigate and notified the Tongren Fuyuan Branch to send laborers to retrieve the body. After examination, the corpse was a stillborn fetus, with the umbilical cord still attached to the navel. However, the placenta had rotted and could not be found. It must have been the stillborn child of a private birth from a nearby family, who was thrown into the sewer to reduce traces. The body was sent to the mortuary. Yesterday morning, the French police reported to the Second Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren to inspect the corpse at the mortuary. It was confirmed that the body was indeed a stillborn female infant, and the court ordered that it be handed over to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for burial.

Women Who Have Abortions Must Be Investigated at the Hospital to See If They Took Medicine to Induce It

Wang Liu Shi, a 33-year-old Anhui woman who lived in the back building of No. 607 Xi Aixiansi Road in the French Concession, carried out the body of her 14-year-old adopted daughter, Xiao Zhen Baozi, who had died of measles, with her husband, Wang Li Bao (39 years old), on the morning of April 23 this year and abandoned it in the open space opposite No. 166 Jufu Road, Xi Aixiansi Road. The police discovered it, sent the body to the mortuary, and reported it to the court for verification. Since the family could not be found, the Shantang charity took custody of the body. Later, the French police found out and arrested the Wang couple and brought them to the Second Special District Court, where they were prosecuted for the crime of abandoning a corpse. As a result, Wang Li Bao was sentenced to six months in prison and is currently serving his term. Wang Liu Shi was acquitted. After being released, she was recommended to work as an amah for a Russian named Fulaifeng Dala (transliteration) at No. 114 Geluoxi Road in the French Concession. Recently, Wang Liu Shi became pregnant for three months. Because of the hard work during the day, the fetus was affected, but it did not miscarry, causing her to feel exhausted and weak. She asked someone to get a prescription for abortion medicine and took it. As a result, her condition worsened and she became unconscious. The Russian employer discovered this and reported it to the French police, who sent her to the Guangci Hospital. The doctor tried to remove the dead fetus from her abdomen, and she was able to escape danger and be safe. She stayed in the hospital to recover. The French police believed that Wang Liu Shi had committed an abortion and sent detectives to bring Liu Shi back to the police station the day before yesterday. Yesterday, she was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. Judge Qiu Huan Ying brought her to trial. The lawyer from the Police Department, Yao Xun Di, stated the case and prosecuted her for the crime of abortion under Article 288 of the Criminal Law. According to Liu Shi's confession, the fetus in her abdomen slipped seven days ago. On the 4th of this month, she passed Hadong Road and met Mr. Yao, who had a fortune-telling stall. She told him about her situation and begged him to prescribe medicine for treatment. He initially refused, saying that someone must be responsible for guaranteeing before he could give a prescription. She then asked her sister, Xue Liu Shi, who lived at No. 12 An'nan Road, to vouch for her. Yao then gave her a prescription. The next day, after taking the medicine, she became unconscious. The employer reported it to the police station and sent her to the hospital. At that time, she had already died and knew nothing. She was saved by the doctor, etc. At this point in the interrogation, the lawyer from the Police Department expressed his opinion, saying that there were key points that needed to be studied. First, whether the prescription taken by the defendant was actually an abortion prescription. Second, to summon the doctor from Guangci Hospital to testify and ask whether the defendant's fetus had already slipped or was induced by taking medicine. The court reported this to the court and ordered a retrial on the 29th. The defendant was exempted from bail and was not allowed to leave her original residence without permission.

The case of the counterfeit coin manufacturing organization at No. 806 Zhoujiazui Road was solved by the Chief Inspectorate, and nine employees of the organization, including Zhang Xueyuan and worker Yang A'gen, were arrested and sent to the First Special District District Court for interrogation, awaiting sentencing. Yesterday, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court. The lawyer from the Public Works Department, Wang Yaotang, filed a public prosecution based on Article 30, Section 2, and Article 195 of the Criminal Law for assisting in the counterfeiting of Chinese national currency and disrupting the financial market, etc., and stated that the case was being heard by Judge Jiang, and the facts were clear, so he requested an adjournment. Questioning Xu Wensheng, he confessed that he was a native of Jiangyin, 31 years old, and a shareholder and manager of Hong Taiyuan Department Store. Together with the Kunshan woman, Sheng Xiaomei, 23 years old, the Pudong woman, Hu A'mei, 18 years old, the Yangzhou woman, Hu Laizi Di, 15 years old, the Wuxi woman, Tang Zhang Shi, 21 years old, and Chen Zhu Shi's daughter, 8-year-old Rui Zhen, were all brought to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. He requested an adjournment for the case and that the four women, Sheng Xiaomei, etc., be sent to the Jiliang Institute for temporary care before their families claim them. According to Sheng Xiaomei, she lived in Zhoujiazhuang, her hometown, and her husband worked in a certain number on Lafayette Road in the French Concession. She came to Shanghai from her hometown on the 18th and met the defendant Chen Ziren on the way. They went to a noodle shop to eat snacks. Hu A'mei said that she was from Bachi Township in Pudong, where her parents and siblings lived at home. A month ago, the defendant Huang Fulin lured her to Zhoupu and took her to his home, where she stayed for about a month. The defendant Chen Dai Shi also came. At that time, she was sent to Dalian as a maid. She did not know anything else. Hu Laizi Di said that she lived in a shack in Yangshupu and was brought to Xiaoshanzi's house by a fat woman in a matchmaking shop. She was sold to the defendant Chen Dai Shi for 60 yuan and lived there for seven days. Both her parents were dead. The defendant Zhang Jinfa also came twice. At that time, she was sent to Dalian as a maid, who said that she could eat well and dress well. Tang Zhang Shi said that she lived at No. 32 Bashan Bridge in the French Concession and used to work in a foreign factory. She had a husband at home. The day before yesterday, the defendant Fan A'xing came and asked her to go to Huangpu Wharf to talk, so she went with him. On the way, she saw him whispering to the defendant Chen Dai Shi, but she did not know what it was about, etc. When questioned, the defendants all gave evasive answers. Judge Xiao Fen Fen ordered that they be detained separately and that the case be investigated and verified at a later date. The four women, Sheng Xiaomei, etc., together with the 8-year-old girl Chen Rui Zhen, were all temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute for temporary care.

Judge's Persuasion Works Wonders: Husband and Wife Reconcile, Divorce Case Ends in Court After Heartfelt Appeals Moved Both Parties

Zhou Zhaogeng, a native of Zhenhai, 28 years old, residing at No. 11, Lane 59, Huade Road, works as a "western boy" (likely a waiter or steward on a ship) at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, earning a monthly salary of 50 to 60 yuan. In 1933, he met Wu Xingdi, a woman from Ningbo, who was 23 years old at the time. They fell in love at first sight. Zhou then engaged a matchmaker, and on March 27 of the same year, they held a formal wedding at the Zhejiang Hotel in Xiaodongmen, Shanghai. Subsequently, he lived with Zhou as a temporary resident in Yichang until April 19 of last year, when he returned with his mother. Recently, Zhou became unemployed, leading to financial difficulties, and the couple often had quarrels. Unable to endure poverty, Wu hired a lawyer to file a petition with the First Special District Local Court requesting permission to divorce Zhou Zhaogeng. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang Yuhai specially opened the 14th Civil Court to investigate. Both the plaintiff and the defendant were present. First, the plaintiff, Wu Xingdi, testified that after marrying Zhou, she gave birth to a child on March 19 of this year. Only a few months later, the defendant often beat and injured her after childbirth. She sought medical treatment, and although she has recovered, it is difficult to live together in the future, so she had no choice but to request a divorce, and so on. The defendant, Zhou Zhaogeng, claimed that he used to work as a "western boy" on a ship, earning 50 to 60 yuan a month. Unexpectedly, the ship recently sailed to Sichuan and was damaged en route, resulting in his unemployment. He has always cherished his wife and has not beaten her. He requested a ruling for them to live together, and so on. Judge Zhang said that arguments and minor matters are inevitable between husband and wife, so why should they rashly divorce? He advised both parties in court to put aside their differences and reconcile. Both the plaintiff and the defendant were moved and expressed their willingness to reconcile, and the case was thus peacefully resolved.

Shanghai Municipal Government's People's Welfare Association Seeks to Relieve Rickshaw Pullers: Establishes Rickshaw Management Office with an Allocated Budget of 50,000 Yuan

According to the Central News Agency, the Municipal Government has established the People's Welfare Affairs Committee to promote the welfare of the common people. The committee believes that in terms of transportation in the city, the operation of rickshaws not only requires safeguarding the livelihoods of tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers but also requires finding ways to improve the technology of rickshaw construction. Therefore, the committee has established a Rickshaw Management Committee to supervise design and other duties and will organize a Rickshaw Management Office to carry out the duties. It is reported that the Rickshaw Management Office will be established soon. The Municipal Government is currently drafting the organizational rules of the Rickshaw Management Office. The position of director will be concurrently held by Xu Peihuang, the director of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau. The office will be divided into technical, inspection, and general affairs sections. In order to facilitate the reorganization, the Municipal Government will allocate 50,000 yuan from the People's Welfare Affairs Fund for initial expenses.

Municipal Ferry: Crew Members Show Courage and Righteousness. A Young Woman Attempts Suicide After an Argument, and a Crew Member Jumps into the Water to Save Her.

At 4:14 PM yesterday, when the Municipal Ferry's Chunbei Line's No. 16 Bolun ferry arrived at the Beijing Road dock, a passenger, Xiao Chen, 23 years old, wearing a pink silk cheongsam, white satin shoes, and flesh-colored stockings, jumped into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. The crew noticed and immediately turned the boat around to catch up. A staff member, Sun Ashu, saw that the person who jumped into the river was still floating on the surface, immediately grabbed a lifebuoy and jumped into the river, pulling the woman's hair to save her. The crew members then used first aid methods, and she soon regained consciousness. She was then sent to the Water Patrol Police Station, where her address was inquired and her family was notified to pick her up. It is reported that the young woman had an argument with her husband the night before, so she suddenly jumped into the river. Fortunately, the Municipal Ferry staff were familiar with the water and jumped into the Huangpu River, and were able to rescue her; otherwise, it would have been impossible to save her.

Collapsed Rickshaw and Tiger Rickshaw Industry Mutual Aid Society Established Yesterday

The Shanghai Collapsed Rickshaw and Tiger Rickshaw Industry Mutual Aid Society convened its founding meeting yesterday at the original site of the New World Great Beijing Opera House. Directors and supervisors were elected. Attendees included Liu Zhongying from the Federation of National Product Manufacturers, Cao Zhigong from the Citizens' Federation, Ge Futian from the Nantong Fellow-Provincials Association, Chen Shude from the Haimen Fellow-Provincials Association, and more than 400 members. Shen Yong, Zou Shisong, Jing Qixiang, Wu Zhengyuan, Yang Chunfu, Chen Baoshan, and Chen Xiaoming served as chairpersons. After the rituals, Chairman Shen Yong delivered the opening speech, saying, "Everyone, we have all come here today with great joy because our request to cancel the additional taxes imposed by the Municipal Council has been satisfactorily resolved. This makes us grateful for the enthusiastic assistance of all sectors of society. At the same time, it also shows that the concession authorities are still able to understand the suffering of our workers. Indeed, given the current situation, with so few passengers and goods, our collapsed rickshaws and tiger rickshaws are already feeling the burden of the original taxes, so how can we bear an increase of 100% and 50% in taxes? Fortunately, the negotiations have gone well, and there will be no further tax increases, so we can temporarily set aside this concern. Furthermore, what does it mean that so many of our colleagues are gathered here today for this meeting? We believe that people in every industry should have a collective organization. With an organization, we can exert our strength; otherwise, we will be scattered and insignificant. The success of our negotiations this time is due, on the one hand, to the enthusiastic assistance of all sectors of society and the understanding of the authorities, and on the other hand, to the united participation and orderly steps of our colleagues. It can be seen that unity and mutual assistance are the most important things for our colleagues. Therefore, we are formally establishing this Mutual Aid Society today to unite our strength and promote the development of our business." Guests then gave speeches. Ge Futian, the representative of the Nantong Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, said, "This time, your colleagues felt that they could not bear the additional taxes imposed by the Public Concession authorities, so they all came to the Fellow-Provincials Association for assistance. Since most of you are fellow provincials, our association naturally has an unshirkable duty. At that time, we sent a special letter to the Shanghai Concession Ratepayers' Association on behalf of your colleagues, explaining your intentions and difficult situation, and requesting them to negotiate and stop the tax increase. It was indeed rare. After receiving the letter, the Ratepayers' Association attached great importance to this case and felt that your industry was in too much distress to withstand the additional taxes, so they put forward a dissenting opinion and demanded that the Municipal Council cancel the agreement to increase taxes. Later, thanks to the righteous words of the Chinese directors and committee members, such as Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Mr. Lin Kanghou, and He Huiban, the wish to cancel the tax increase was realized. Your industry was able to reduce its burden, and the Fellow-Provincials Association is very pleased. Now that your colleagues have taken a further step to seek permanent unity and have formally established a Mutual Aid Society, and the number of participants is so enthusiastic, the future is certainly unlimited. However, I feel that there is no end to the affairs of society. After your association is established today, there will naturally be many tasks that everyone will work together to do, such as how to seek the development of the industry, improve livelihoods, and other matters for the public good of the industry. Therefore, in addition to congratulating you on your success here today, I hope that everyone will uphold the spirit of unity and mutual assistance, work hard, and strive to achieve the final mutual benefit." (Speeches by Liu Shenying, Chen Jiufeng, etc. are omitted)

(2) Resolved on how to express gratitude for the Municipal Council's cancellation of the tax increase.
