The Site of the Former Xiamen Road Western Jail Will Be Used to Build a Fire Department Building: Funds Are Not Yet Available, but the Principle Has Been Decided.

At the regular meeting of the Municipal Council Board of Directors on the 24th of this month, it was decided in principle to designate the site of the former Xiamen Road Western Jail for the construction of the Central Fire Department. However, issues such as the architectural style, volume, and construction of other houses were temporarily postponed, and Messrs. Kenei, Gillanley, and Zhanbu were elected to form a committee to investigate the organization and funding of the Fire Department.

Construction Plan

It is found that the construction of the Western section of the Huade Road Prison will be completed soon. The Xiamen Road West half will be moved in immediately. The old houses left behind, due to years of disrepair, will be demolished. Therefore, the director of the Fire Department has suggested building a new building on the site as the central station. According to the Fire Department Director's submission, after the completion of the central station in the future, there should be a large machine room, so that the existing central station and branch stations on Tiantong Road and Xinzha Road can be moved in. Eight stories of dormitories and residences should be built above the machine room to accommodate firefighters and their families. It is also planned to build another general office building with a total of seven floors, including a special machine room for the installation of special equipment and ambulances, as well as alarm bells, electrical rooms, training rooms, and dormitories. In addition, there are workshops, storage rooms, and dormitories for Chinese staff and their families.

Costs

Since this plan was proposed by the director of the Fire Department and discussed by the Security Committee, the director of the Public Works Department immediately expressed his opinion, stating that the Fire Department's equipment was developing too quickly and the costs were increasing too much. If all the houses were built according to the Fire Department Director's plan, the total cost would be 3 million yuan, not including interest. Therefore, according to his proposal, it is proposed to first build a central fire department building, the size of which should be twice the total of the existing stations. All other construction will be discussed after the central station is established in the future.

Extraordinary Development

The director of the Finance Department also felt that the Fire Department's equipment showed a phenomenon of extraordinary development, and said that whether the staff of the department could be reduced should be investigated. He generally agreed with the proposal of the director of the Public Works Department. However, the director of the Fire Department said that the development of the Fire Department seemed to be too fast, but this was actually because the department's effectiveness was established too late. Therefore, he could only partially agree with the proposal of the director of the Public Works Department.

Principle Approved

In principle, according to the plan of the director of the Fire Department, a central fire department building will be built, with a total of nine floors, requiring a total construction cost of 1 million yuan. If the number of dormitories and residences on the upper floors can be reduced, the cost can be saved by 200,000 yuan. According to the opinion of the director of the Public Works Department, this plan is not too extravagant, because the situation of the existing stations is very crowded. In the future, when the new building is established, all stations will be moved in, accounting for three-quarters of the area of the new building, and only one-quarter will be reserved for future business expansion. However, the director of the Finance Department stated that it was impossible to raise such a large expenditure in this year's budget, and expressed concern about the expansion of the Fire Department's expenses, hoping that the department could reduce its administration and save money. At that time, the chairman stated that before there was any certainty about the financial issues, it seemed unnecessary to discuss the detailed rules for the construction of the central fire department building in depth. However, in order to allow the director of the Public Works Department to foresee what the site of the former Xiamen Road Western Jail would be used for in the future, so as to engage in design, it was decided to first stipulate in principle that the site would be designated for the construction of the central fire department. All other matters were temporarily postponed. This decision has been recommended by the Committee on Public Utilities to the Board of Directors, and the Board of Directors has expressed its agreement.

Chinese Ratepayers Write to Municipal Council on Behalf of Rickshaw Pullers' Association, Requesting Three Matters Be Given Special Consideration to Accord with the Purpose of Establishing a Mutual Aid Society

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association sent a letter to Mr. Felippo, Acting General Manager of the Shanghai Public Concession, saying, "Dear Sir, we have received a letter from the Shanghai Special District Public Rickshaw Pullers' Association, which states: 'In order to improve the organization, our association has elected a delegation of members, and the delegation has elected 110 people as directors to form the board of directors. We are now submitting the list of directors for your review and requesting that you ask the Municipal Council to implement the following three matters: (1) The new directors of the Public Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society should be established on August of this year and implement projects that directly benefit the rickshaw pullers. (2) The relief funds for August should be retained and decided after the new board of directors is established. (3) He Wushan, a rickshaw puller representative who was detained on official business, should be rescued and the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society should find a way to bail him out. The reasons for the above three items are as follows: (1) The organization of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society, as the name suggests, should be based on the rickshaw pullers themselves. During the transition period, it is okay to ask for outside help. The directors of the Municipal Council, in view of the fact that the original directors' distribution was too unrepresentative of public opinion, agreed to reorganize on June 24 of this year. Therefore, the original directors should immediately transfer the accounts and other items. Moreover, the original board of directors has been running for more than 10 months, and the transfer procedures are not complicated. One month is more than enough to handle the procedures, but they deliberately delay, are reluctant to leave, and obstruct the progress, harming the interests of the rickshaw pullers who paid. The Municipal Council resolved to reorganize on June 24, and the order has already been issued, but the original board of directors deliberately delays, which is a clear violation of the Municipal Council's order. If the new board of directors delays taking over, the money contributed by the rickshaw pullers may be wasted. Even with various improvements and good implementation, they may not be able to promote it. (2) All the relief funds of the Mutual Aid Society have been collected for 12 months. Now that the association has been ordered to reorganize, the relief funds for August should be taken care of by the rickshaw business association and retained by the collecting bank, and then decided after the new board of directors is formally established. (3) He Wushan, a rickshaw puller propagandist of the Public Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society who was detained on official business, has already completed the public prosecution part. He is now detained for private prosecution, and the court ordered him to pay bail, but he has not been released because he cannot find a guarantor. The Rickshaw Committee of the Municipal Council should order the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society to find a way to bail him out, provide relief, and clarify right and wrong. Thinking that the Municipal Council established the Rickshaw Committee and implemented the 13 new articles to improve the treatment of rickshaw pullers out of humanitarianism, and specially appointed Maxi, Zhu Maocheng, and Wang Zhiren as members to specialize in this matter, the reason is that these three people are kind-hearted, exhausted their efforts, managed it, and achieved success. Countless rickshaw pullers have improved their treatment and received benefits. The rickshaw puller representatives have repeatedly submitted petitions and offered opinions, which have been adopted, and have been recognized as the official representatives of the rickshaw pullers. Zhu Maocheng sent letters to the leaders of the representatives, Cang Gongwen, Xu Zhulin, Zhu Fengxiang, and He Wushan, to specialize in publicity work, distribute leaflets printed by Zhu Maocheng to resist the capitalists, and instruct them to organize a petition group to support the committee, which resulted in troublemakers from unknown sources letting out the tires of rickshaws along the way and blaming the rickshaw puller representatives, resulting in their arrest by the police and trial by the court. Fortunately, the great philanthropist Zhu Shuqiao made efforts to rescue them, so that they were also detained. Fortunately, social enthusiasts such as Yu Gongqiaqing came forward to explain and released all those detained, sentencing only He Wushan to three months in prison. He Wushan refused to accept the appeal and was sentenced to three years of probation. He appealed again and the original sentence was upheld, resulting in execution. The fact that He Wushan was sentenced contains injustice and is indescribable, and the three months of imprisonment he suffered was due to official business. At present, the term of imprisonment has expired. For the private prosecution part, the court requires a shop to provide a guarantee, but He Wushan is a rickshaw puller, so how can he find a guarantor? The philanthropist Zhu Gongshuqiao, who had made efforts in the past, has already passed away. He Wushan suffered injustice for the public good and for the sake of the Rickshaw Committee. The Rickshaw Committee should be responsible for finding a guarantor to release him. More than ten days have passed, and he is still detained. However, Zhu Maocheng, the Rickshaw Committee, and Zhang Dengying, the secretary-general of the Mutual Aid Society, turned a deaf ear and did not think of rescuing him. Where is the original intention of establishing the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society? Furthermore, Zhang Dengying, the secretary-general, is supported by the rickshaw pullers and receives a salary of 320 yuan per month, but he still claims to be fulfilling his obligations. He does not know how to be grateful. He does not think of rescuing his subordinate rickshaw puller propagandist, who has suffered such injustice. The intention of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society is to do what it wants. Therefore, we hereby send a letter to the directors of your association, requesting that they examine and handle the matter, which will be a great merit.'" Because of the foregoing reasons, the letter was received. It is found that the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society was established for the benefit of the rickshaw pullers and is maintained by the rickshaw pullers' sweat and blood. The Municipal Council should give special consideration to the opinions of the rickshaw pullers in order to conform to the purpose of establishing the Mutual Aid Society. We send you a copy of the list of directors of the association for your reference and request that you expedite the handling of the matter. This is to Mr. Felippo, Acting General Manager of the Shanghai Public Concession.

Death of Female Doctor Tang Meilin

Dr. Tang Meilin, a pediatrician, was both academically excellent and benevolent. She practiced medicine at the Sino-French Pharmacy for more than twenty years, saving countless lives. She did not care about consultation fees for the poor and sick, and her support for the cultivation of children from poor families was particularly beneficial to society. She recently suffered a heart attack and, despite the best efforts of famous doctors, she was unable to recover and unfortunately passed away on the 16th of this month. Those who heard the news sighed with regret that another senior female doctor in Shanghai had passed away.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Zheng Yimei)

Modern women, in this summer, often wear pure white gloves, covering their jade hands, while their feet are barefoot, without socks. What is abundant there is diminished here. Observing this further strengthens my belief.

The asphalt road is wet with rain, and the road is bright and shiny, like a mirror. Cars and horses pass over it, and their reflections are clearly visible. Illuminated by neon lights at night, it is even more colorful. This is also a symbol of material civilization.

When going out, the weather seems sunny and rainy, which is most hateful. If you bring rain gear and the sun suddenly shines, you will feel that what you are carrying is extremely cumbersome. If you don't bring rain gear and a shower suddenly falls, you will be drenched all over and unable to move. However, this kind of situation is not what the automobile class talks about.

Kunshan is very close to Shanghai, but it is impossible to enjoy the conjoined lotus planted by Gu Zhongying, not to mention the pines of Huangshan, the elms of Luofu, the peonies of Luoyang, and the cherry blossoms of Yingdao. Perhaps it is because I am vulgar that heaven deliberately withholds the blessing of sight!

When I hold the pen to write essays, I often see the beautiful neighbor dressing up and standing leisurely by the railing. However, I dare not engage in fantasies, so I hang a picture of a beauty on the wall to look at, and then everything returns to illusion and silence.

Watching movies and dramas and watching Peking opera differ in the newness of their minds by at least a century.

Record of the Martyr Jin Liang

— Tiansheweng

I'm afraid that we won't find a martyr nowadays. In the decades before, it was common to hear and see in the society. Therefore, in miscellaneous books and notes, there are often records of the facts of martyrs. This is not the brush and ink of literati who love things, but it is indeed an indelible fact. Today, when the new morality has not been completed, I think that these old moralities such as "loyalty," "filial piety," "festival," "righteousness," "diligence," and "thrift" should not be overthrown. Chairman Chiang's advocacy of "new life" is indeed an urgent task today.

Sixty or seventy years ago, a towering martyr was born in my hometown. The style of chastity is enough to illuminate the ages. Now the tomb of the martyr is located on the north bank of Cihu. The people of the town go to worship her in spring and autumn. In order to promote the potential virtue, I wrote it out to shame the women of the world who have no chastity!

The martyr Jin Liang's husband was a fisherman who had been a guest in other ports for a long time and never returned. Her mother-in-law was a woman who rented out pearl flower jewelry and was licentious by nature. Although she was a widow, she was familiar with a pawnshop clerk in the city. The martyr was very dissatisfied with her mother-in-law's behavior and often advised her honestly, but her mother-in-law refused to listen. On the contrary, she was concerned about her daughter-in-law's eyes and ears and was afraid of spreading the word, which would affect her own reputation. So she discussed with her adulterer and came up with a method of "going with the flow." The adulterer was very happy to hear this. It was like killing two birds with one stone and enjoying the beauty. So he often tempted the martyr in every possible way and used sweet words to seduce her. Who knew that the martyr was as beautiful as a peach and plum and as cold as frost? Not only did the clerk have an unpleasant time and was scolded severely, but even her mother-in-law was ridiculed. Her mother-in-law had no other way to deal with it and became angry with shame. At first, she still used coercive means, but it was still ineffective. Later, she imprisoned her in the cellar and often used red-hot pliers to scald her lower body indiscriminately. Over time, her lower body was scorched and rotten, and there was no complete skin. The miserable pain and crying made people sour. Later, the neighbors all complained and, while her mother-in-law was out, they entered the house, opened the cellar, and saw that the martyr could no longer move and her lower body was festering and unbearable to look at. So they used a tatami to lift her to the county government to extend her grievances. The county official was very angry and arrested the adulterer and adulteress and punished them according to law. The martyr was promoted to the county, did not say a word, and then died. The people of the town admired her integrity and buried her bones on the shore of Cihu outside Beiguo and wrote "Tomb of the Martyr Jin Liang" in numbers.

— Tongfu

What I can't see is a heart that leaps before the date!

The Frog Almost Came from Huangshan

— Jiang Danshu

I read a news report in this newspaper on July 8, which stated: "A terrible sound inside Xiaobang in Pudong's Qinciyang Temple! A big green frog scared many villagers to death. A brave man, Chen, caught it, and the people's hearts were greatly settled. The four feet stretched out about a foot long, and when it called, it roared like an angry ox, and the sound vibrated for miles." I am not a naturalist, and I am certainly not a detective in the animal world, but I can conclude that this frog came from Huangshan in Huizhou or places like Huangshan. Seven out of ten, there is a poem to prove it!

The first time I saw the face of Huangshan, I learned to be like Tai Zhen. The cinnabar particles are refreshing, and the flowing water is always new. I brought up the Wu costume dance, and my ears heard the vibration of the frog drums. I washed away the dust and also thought about it, as if I were a citizen of Getian!

This is the impromptu poem I recited last year on this day when I visited Huangshan, after taking a hot spring bath under the thatched shed (Ziyun Temple). What is meant by "hearing the frog drums vibrate"? As soon as we arrived at Huangshan, we took a hot spring bath that we had never taken before in our lives. This hot spring is a cinnabar spring, not a sulfur spring. The taste of the touch on the skin is truly indescribable. At this time, just when the setting sun was in the mountains and the breeze was blowing gently, there was a large stream next to the spring. At that time, it was a great drought, and the water in the stream was very small. Only jagged rocks were seen, and the sound of a majestic "boom boom" suddenly started in the east, and a majestic "boom boom" sound started in the west, just like the appearance of an ox roaring in the article above. At first, I couldn't guess what the sound was. So I asked the porter we hired locally: What is this strange sound? He replied: It's a frog calling! Asked: Is the worm sound so loud? Answer: This is a "rock frog." I'm used to hearing it here! Asked: How big is it? Answer: Very, very big, several times bigger than ordinary field chickens! In such a question and answer, I didn't realize that the dusk was gradually closing, and the moonlight suddenly opened. "Boom boom boom boom," sang in the east and echoed in the west. This courageous and energetic sound is enough to make people get up and dance when they hear field chickens, and even more to make people think of the aspirations of King Goujian of Yue, who used an angry frog to encourage the army in those days. Unfortunately, today's angry frog is both ignored by few people and does not know how to love itself. It also wants to take advantage of the trend to come to Shanghai to see the mundane world, but it does not know how to ask about the customs when entering the country. It happened to land on the shore of the semi-rural Pudong first, and it is inevitable that it will be considered a "savage head" by the unheard-of workers and detained. Its life is in danger! If it comes to Puxi as soon as it arrives, this magnificent "boom boom" sound will surely resonate with the city tiger, and it will not suffer this misfortune. I think the fact is that there have been floods everywhere recently, and the rapids in that stream will surely rush to the river, then rush to the river, and the three rushes will lead to all directions. The big green frog, who is full of travel interest, will also linger and forget to return and ride the long wind and break the ten thousand miles of waves! This big frog sound has not only been heard by the people of Pudong, but also by me, who likes to travel to famous mountains and rivers, and has not heard it anywhere else. Even in Huangshan, it seems that I have never heard it when staying by the stream in his temple.

Chatter

Relief Efforts in Suzhou

— Qingyun

Relief efforts in Suzhou, in these economically depressed times, have seen significant improvements since Zhang Yipeng and Zhu Guanyi took charge of the various organizations under the jurisdiction of the Relief Institute, showing much progress compared to before. The charitable organizations under the Suzhou Relief Institute include five institutions: the Old People's Home, the Reformatory and Vocational Training Center, the Infant Nursery, the Changshan Bureau, and the School for the Deaf and Mute. As for the "Orphanage" outside Changmen, it is run by local people and not under the jurisdiction of the Relief Institute.

The "Old People's Home" is located at Pujiqiao bank of Xiatang Street in Shantang Street, formerly known as "Pujitang," which was specifically for beggars. However, the regulations used to be very lenient, and beggars could come and go freely. The more upright ones would go to the streets every day to peddle licorice medicine cakes and tung oil ash, without being taught any skills. But now, there has been a major reform. Inmates are absolutely not allowed to go out, except those who sell tung oil ash and are allowed to go to the streets for business. The internal facilities, such as clothing, food, and accommodation, have all been improved, and the inmates are also taught to make shoes, knit towels, and other profitable businesses. Compared to the previous "begging Pujitang," it is indeed a world apart.

The Reformatory and Vocational Training Center is located in Baijia Lane, Loumen. The buildings are large and clean. Those being reformed are divided into two categories: self-funded and publicly funded. The self-funded ones have more comfortable food and accommodation. The inmates there must take six classes in rotation from 8:00 a.m. to 3:00 p.m. every day, and the rest of the time is for work. The work sections there include rattan work, charcoal base, spinning, and wood machine departments, as well as scripture copying and gardening, a total of six types. Teaching is tailored to the individual, such as letting scholars copy scriptures and farmers till the land, each finding their place. After work, the inmates also have entertainment, such as ping-pong and outdoor sports, to relieve the mental and physical fatigue after a day's work.

Among the charitable organizations under the Relief Institute, the most profitable is undoubtedly the Changshan Bureau, which provides coffin storage. Although the Changshan Bureau also has public coffin storage for a few dollars a year, the ordinary coffin storage rooms, with three coffins in a room, cost 50 yuan per room per year, and a single room costs 70 yuan per year. Furthermore, the Changshan Bureau has so many buildings, so the annual income is considerable. According to the Bureau's report, the surplus in half a year, after deducting expenses, was more than 2,000 yuan. Director Zhang saw that the funeral business could make a lot of money, so he used the three large halls where coffins entered the hall at the Changshan Bureau, whitewashed them, and converted them into funeral parlors. However, this is still a fledgling business, and no one has patronized it yet!

The Infant Nursery, formerly known as the Infant Hall, is located in Zhongyou Jixiang Lane, Loumen. The infants there are, of course, abandoned children. The infants in the nursery are divided into two sections: those fed with human milk and those fed with cow's milk. If someone is willing to take them out for feeding, that is also possible. Each infant is given a subsidy of 6 yuan and 40 cents per month for feeding expenses. The children there all sleep in specially made rattan beds, and their clothing and food are managed using scientific methods, so the infants live much longer than before. If someone adopts the infants as their children, the amount of feeding expenses is determined by age, with a minimum of 4 yuan per infant.

The School for the Deaf and Mute in Song Xianzhou Lane, although established not long ago, has very impressive student achievements. A few days ago, the school held a graduation ceremony, and the three students demonstrated calligraphy and painting to the guests, all of which were excellent. This alone proves that the school's teaching achievements are indeed commendable!

Xiaoxitian (Little Western Paradise)

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Sixteen: The Curtain Conceals Tearful Traces, Though Escaping Cold Looks; Fine Clothes Flaunt Fortune, Having Been to Powerful Doors

Li Shilian said, "Brother Jie Fu never lies, there's no need to prove it. But I don't know what task Commissioner Lan has here." Zhang Jiefu took the mandarin jacket on the tea table, tucked it under his arm, grabbed his hat, and put it on his head, not caring that it was tilted to one side. He raised his head and walked outside, saying, "Who knows what he's here to do? But according to my ideal, he'll probably be here for ten days or half a month. He's a central commissioner, and if I can get his approval to write a letter to any organization, ha! The hope must be great. Tea boy, open the door and make tea for me." As he spoke, his voice was very high. In fact, the tea boy had already opened the door and made tea. He walked into the room, and Li Shilian followed him in. Smiling, he said, "I was just talking to Mr. Cheng next door, saying that Mr. Zhang's talent is really a head above anyone else. Those who came to Xi'an with him have no news at all, but he is watching a good job come into his hands." Zhang Jiefu raised his head and said with a smile, "I wouldn't dare say I'm talented, luck is what determines everything. If Mr. Lan hadn't come himself, I could say I was confident in finding a way out." Li Shilian said, "I've long wanted to treat you to a pot of wine, I have a lot to talk about. Commissioner Lan is coming tomorrow, I'm afraid you won't have time, can we go out to a small restaurant now and have a good time?" Jie Fu smiled and said, "I wouldn't dare to bother you." Li Shilian laughed and said, "What are you talking about? We're brothers, you bother me once, I bother you once, that's nothing. If you don't honor me, you can call me a bastard." Zhang Jiefu hadn't replied yet, when someone laughed and walked in from outside the door, saying, "Why is Mr. Li admitting to being that thing!" This misunderstanding made Li Shilian unbearably embarrassed. (275)

Records of Fragrant Imperial Incense

— Original Author Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

"Now that he's the governor of a province," the Empress Dowager said, "his rank is already very, very high; everyone will naturally respect him, there's absolutely no need for him to put on any airs himself. Especially since he's already a representative of the court, he should always think for the court in everything he does. If he sees these two points, he will definitely treat his people with great leniency! If that old beggar rushed through in front of his ceremonial guard, the most appropriate method would have been to tell his retainers to walk a little slower, let the old beggar pass safely; afterwards, he could still supervise the local officials and yamen runners, instructing them to be careful to clear the way in the future. If he hadn't let his retainers whip the old beggar, nor stopped his ceremonial guard, then the old beggar would have inevitably been trampled to death by the cavalry, which would not have been the best policy. He doesn't even know how to adapt to the situation in such trivial matters, how can he go out and be some high-ranking official?"

The sixth charge, secretly concealing tributes from various regions, can be said to be the most serious. In fact, the people who reported it were not the people of Guangdong, but the provincial officials. Because in the era of autocracy, there was a custom that no matter where one discovered something extremely valuable and of excellent quality;—whether it was a piece of jade of unparalleled purity and clarity, or just a pair of unusually beautiful golden pheasants—the local government would go to great lengths to find it and use it as tribute to the Emperor or Empress Dowager. But their official rank was too low to directly offer it to the imperial court, so all tributes had to be passed on by the provincial governors-general. (375)

Davis Cup Inter-Zone Final: USA Wins Over Germany 4-1

Amazing Performance by American Budge, Defeats Kramm 3-1

(London, 24th Reuters) In the Davis Cup Inter-Zone Final, the United States, already leading 2-1, saw Germany completely defeated in the final two singles matches today. As a result, the United States won 4-1 overall. Starting this Saturday, they will compete against England in the Challenge Round.

Budge's victory over Kramm was the most unexpected. Beforehand, it was widely predicted that victory was extremely unlikely. In the first set, Budge completely lost. In the second set, he counterattacked desperately, causing Kramm to be indecisive. In the third set, Kramm led 5-2, but Budge scored three consecutive points and won 8-6. In the final set, Kramm was again ahead 3-1, but Budge then won five consecutive games and won the fourth set 6-3.

England vs. United States Challenge Round: To be held at Wimbledon starting on Saturday. Doubles on Monday, final two singles on Tuesday. The lineups are as follows:

(England) Singles: Perry, Austin. Doubles: Hughes, Tuckey.

(United States) Singles: Budge, Wood. Doubles: Allison, Van Ryn.

China: Establishment of the Mathematical Society of China Yesterday

Speeches by Chairman Hu Dunfu, Li Zhaohuan, and Others

The Ministry of Education Specially Sends Chen Kezhong to the Meeting to Give Instructions

Meetings to Continue Today and Tomorrow to Discuss Society Affairs

The Mathematical Society of China, organized by professors from various universities in the country, has been prepared and was officially established yesterday at the Jiaotong University Library. The opening ceremony was held in the morning, and the articles of association were discussed in the afternoon. Meetings will continue today and tomorrow to discuss and review issues and terminology. The details are as follows:

Attendees: Over forty members, including Hu Dunfu, Gu Yangwu, Yuan Bingnan, Qiu Weiyu, Chen Huaishu, Shi Faren, and Hu Gangfu from Jiaotong University; Zhu Gongjin from Guanghua University; Ma Mengqiang from Henan University; Xiong Dizi from Tsinghua University; Chen Jinmin and Zheng Jianhan from Jinan University; He Lu from Chongqing University; Zhang Zhenqian from Guangxi University; Gao Yangzhi from Datong University; Chen Jiangong from Zhejiang University; and Dong Xingbei from Wuhan University. Chen Kezhong, representative of the Ministry of Education, and Li Zhaohuan, representative of Jiaotong University, and Yang Xiaoshu, representative of the Science Society of China, attended as advisors.

Chairman's Report: Hu Dunfu was elected as Chairman, and Yuan Bingnan as Secretary. The Chairman began by reporting that the idea of establishing the Mathematical Society of China had existed for a long time. He recalled that Mr. Zhou Meiquan of the mathematical community had generously donated many mathematical books more than a decade ago and expressed his willingness to donate funds if the Mathematical Society were established. However, due to subsequent changes in the political situation, the idea was shelved. Until last year, Mr. He Lu came to Shanghai from Sichuan and strongly advocated for the organization of the Mathematical Society. The Science Society of China also believed that since various specialized societies had been established one after another, it was necessary to organize a Mathematical Society. Therefore, colleagues were gathered to start preparations, and after several discussions by the preparatory committee, the society was established today. In the future, the work will be divided and cooperated with the Science Society of China to seek progress.

Instructions from the Ministry of Education: Chen Kezhong, representative of the Ministry of Education, gave instructions, stating that Chinese science can be divided into three major periods: (1) the late Qing dynasty, (2) the early Republic of China, and (3) the last ten years. Scientific knowledge was very superficial in the first period, so there was nothing to talk about. Although there were many people in the second period, they were divided by different schools of thought, which was a period of division. In the third period, not only has the number of people increased dramatically, but everyone is working hard and can unite, which is a good phenomenon. Looking at the establishment of various societies, the astronomical and geological societies were the earliest, followed by physics and chemistry. The botanical and zoological societies were also established last year, and this year comes the Mathematical Society. The Mathematical Society is the mother of all sciences, and it is hoped that colleagues will work harder, surpass those who came before, and become the crown jewel of all sciences.

Speeches by Guests: Next were speeches by guests: (1) Li Zhaohuan, President of Jiaotong University, said that mathematics is the oldest science in the world, and this university is also the oldest university in Shanghai. Moreover, this university has always emphasized science and regards it as a fundamental subject. Therefore, he, on behalf of all teachers and students, sincerely welcomes the Society. Mathematics is the mother of all sciences, and the establishment of the Mathematical Society will be of great benefit to the future of science. (2) Yang Xiaoshu of the Science Society of China said that the establishment of various societies in the past two or three years shows the rapid progress of Chinese science. However, thirty or forty years ago, there was no science in China, only the terms Chinese learning and Western learning. Scientific terms only appeared at the end of the Qing dynasty. The Science Society of China was established twenty years ago and can be said to be the earliest scientific research institution. Now, societies for applied science and natural science are springing up, which shows that China now has this talent and this science. The establishment of the Mathematical Society establishes a new force in the academic community, concentrates talent, and will surely add a unique brilliance to the mathematical community. The meeting adjourned at around 11 a.m.

Discussion of the Articles of Association: At 12 noon, Li Zhaohuan, President of Jiaotong University, hosted a banquet for all the attending members at the faculty and staff club. The meeting continued at 2 p.m. to discuss the articles of association. Hu Dunfu remained as Chairman, and Yuan Bingnan as Secretary. After a long time, the articles were finally amended and passed, and the meeting ended at around 3 p.m.

Continuation of the Meeting Today: The meeting will continue today from 10 a.m. The meeting will discuss society affairs in the morning, elect officers in the afternoon, read papers tomorrow morning, and review the mathematical terms proposed by the Ministry of Education tomorrow afternoon. In the evening, members in Shanghai will host a public banquet for all members. The conference will then conclude.

The Municipal Deans of Students and Civics Teachers Qualification Review Committee, in order to assess the deans of students and civics teachers who have passed the review and been hired by various middle schools, requires them to report on their work in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the Central Committee. The committee has already issued a notice to comply. The committee has now sent a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau requesting that it be circulated to the principals of various schools. The original letter reads: "To the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau: In accordance with Article 12 of the Regulations on the Review of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civics Teachers in Secondary Schools promulgated by the Central Executive Committee, all deans of students and civics teachers who have passed the review shall, after being hired by the school, submit a summary of their work to the Committee for Review of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civics Teachers at least once every semester for assessment. This committee issued an order to all incumbent deans of students and civics teachers in the city on May 3rd of this year, requiring them to report on their work in the school at least once every semester for assessment, starting this semester. Now that the semester has ended for some time, many schools have complied with the order and submitted reports, but there are still some who have not. Therefore, we are writing to request your bureau to notify the principals of various middle schools in the city to instruct the deans of students and civics teachers in their respective schools to promptly submit their work summaries for assessment. This is of utmost importance."

Free Talk

Summer Chat

— Feng Zi

About two months ago, I read a long article by Mr. Gu Shao called "Poetry Talk." Because I disagreed with his understanding of poetry—especially Yuan Zicai's poetry—I once wrote an article in this publication called "Starting from Poetry and Reality." Not long after this article was published, I returned to my hometown due to illness. When I returned to Shanghai, I learned from a friend that Mr. Zhou had published a reply in Qingguang. When I looked at it, the title was "On Poetry Valuing Subtlety," and the issue had been diverted.

Mr. Zhou first assumed that I had not carefully read his proposed argument, because he "was discussing poetry talk and did not mention a single word about poetry, but I forcibly dragged him into poetry." But then he said:

"I believe that poetry is conceived in the mind and is not about meticulous textual refinement. Meticulous refinement of words and phrases, like Jia Changjiang's 'three sentences taking two years to achieve, one sigh causing tears to flow,' is enough to hinder the life and progress of poetry. Therefore, new poetry resolutely advocates abandoning tonal patterns and rhyme schemes to break free from the shackles of old poetry; this is the meaning of my short essay."

This can be considered a slap in the face. It turns out that the "short essay" did also mention poetry. However, to be honest, I only knew that Mr. Zhou was vigorously promoting the mind, but I did not see that he also advocated breaking free from constraints. Even now, when I reread that article, I still cannot see it. I am truly "unfortunate."

Mr. Zhou borrowed phrases from Suiyuan (Yuan Mei), not only without quotation marks but also with modifications, which shows that he originally intended to present them as his own opinions. But this time, he declared them to be Suiyuan's words again. When expressing personal opinions, there may be some discrepancies, and Suiyuan naturally cannot intervene. But when the person quoting extracts unimportant aspects, it shows that they originally failed to understand it.

The following are my opinions:

I once said: "Only that which does not obscure reality, does not distort reality, and can fully utilize real-world data is good poetry." The sentence before your eyes is about the quality of poetry, not about whether someone is a poet or not. If the "mind" school wants to regard something like "a river is like a standing coffin" as poetry, I can do nothing about it; however, I can say that it is not good poetry.

Du Fu seems to be an exposing poet, but not all of his poems use real-world data; Li Bai, although a drunken fool "indulging beyond physical constraints," also has good poetry that does not obscure reality. This requires deep thought from the reader. If you want to extract good poetry from the Suiyuan Poetry Collection, I think you should first select "Weicao Lament" and many works depicting scenery, because this is precisely his important aspect, and these poems are connected to reality. His poems for a certain Mr. and Mrs. when his "mind" surges are definitely not of high quality. I have said before that Suiyuan's advocacy of the mind is only a tool to oppose traditional thought, and is not comparable to today's mind-reversing homebodies. Hong Liangji said: "Yuan Daling Mei's poetry is like a celestial fox, revealing its tail when drunk." This can be said to be a sound argument.

Finally, I want to mention the main point of Mr. Zhou's proposed argument this time. I have never advocated any "straight" literature, and I don't even know what "curved" and "straight" are. If that refers to the hidden and obvious in the method of performance, the direct narrative and the side writing, then it is entirely a question of the method of performance, and has nothing to do with reality, mind, and so on. The method of expression can vary from person to person, from matter to matter, and from place to place. Essays do not necessarily value straightness, and poems do not necessarily value subtlety. Essays with indirect narratives and poems with direct narratives can still be good essays and good poems.

The "good" that I am talking about here refers to the poetry and prose itself and its effect. Poetry and prose that like to tell jokes and interfere in other people's business may not be good in my opinion. I believe that the meaning of the word "good" is not so elusive.

These are all just idle talk, used to beat the summer heat. If I can only be considered a writer because of this, then I don't need to seek the admiration of others.

A Pair

— Qian Dong

A misty rain. The night is already very late. There are no pedestrians on the road. A patrolman suddenly appeared from the corner of the road.

His upright body was wrapped in a new blue uniform, so blue that it shimmered under the streetlights. The leather shoes made a strange noise. His eyes followed the sound of the leather shoes, gliding along very smartly.

He was getting closer and closer, and his eyes had already slid over to the young man in a suit standing on the curb. In the dark, gloomy night air, the man was flicking the ash off his blood-red cigarette with his finger.

He walked towards the young man in the suit. Before he had carefully sized up the other person's appearance, he exclaimed:

"You…"

"No," the young man in the suit took a hard puff of his cigarette, then slowly continued while rotating the bright ring on his ring finger with his thumb, "Please don't suspect me. I am waiting here for a friend from ten years ago."

"Ten years ago, my friend and I often came here for tea (he pointed behind him with his thumb). It used to be called Longxing Teahouse, but now it has been changed to a half-teahouse, half-snack shop. I saw it during the day."

"My friend and I were together all day long, talking about how to make a living, how to avoid starving."

"But we were always hungry, so we either sat in teahouses all day or wandered the streets. Yes, we would never be alone anywhere. Because we were poor, we were lonely, and we needed comfort and support even more. So, when other friends saw me, they always called us 'a pair!' 'Here comes that pair again.'" He laughed, and a few gold teeth flashed.

He took another hard drag on the cigarette butt, threw it on the ground, wiped his mouth, and continued:

"You don't have anything to do, do you? Then let's talk for a while. Once, ten years ago today, I had no way to survive in this city, so I decided to go to the docks and try my luck."

"It was also him who helped me plan a little travel money, although he strongly opposed me leaving him. That night, we also drank there (he looked at the shop across the street, which was separated by a light rain). That wine shop is probably closed now. We drank until the wine shop closed, which was half past two in the morning, I remember very clearly (he stretched out his left hand and looked at the watch on his wrist). We made a pact at the time, to meet here again on this day ten years later, no matter how difficult it was, we had to find a way to meet. Right now (he looked at his watch again) it's one twenty-five. He hasn't come yet. I guess, as long as he's still alive, he'll come. When he sees that I'm still alive, he'll surely exclaim, 'You, you're not dead yet!' Yes, as long as he's still alive, he'll definitely come."

"So, where have you been these past ten years?"

"Places? I've been all over the place, quite a few places if you count them up. Tianjin, Jilin, Beijing, ×××, almost everywhere."

"What kind of business have you been doing in these places?"

"A lot. Tea business, restaurants, and recently even a mining business." He stretched out his left hand again, revealing the shiny watch, and it was almost one forty.

"So, you're very successful now?" The patrolman asked flatly, and without waiting for a reply, walked away.

"Yes," the young man in the suit replied casually. He sent the patrolman away with a proud look, and the patrolman disappeared at a corner.

A moment later, a figure came running from the corner where the patrolman had turned. He was also wearing a suit, with a yellow raincoat over it. As he ran, he shouted loudly to the young man in the suit standing on the curb:

"Lao Hui! Lao Hui!"

The man called Lao Hui also waved his arms wildly to greet him. They met and naturally shook hands tightly.

"Lao Hui, you're not dead yet!"

"And you? You're not dead either! Hahaha!"

"Let's go!" He tugged at Lao Hui's sleeve, then pinched the material of the sleeve and laughed, "Pig! You must be on a lucky streak, wearing such fine clothes."

"Hahaha! They're very cheap! What about you? Your clothes aren't bad either!"

They walked and laughed. Two long shadows swayed in the night rain behind them.

"Where shall we go?" Lao Hui asked.

"I've already prepared a car, just a few more steps, at that corner, I told him to wait. Tonight, I'm definitely going to take you to play with some girls!"

"Lao Jiu! No!" Lao Hui suddenly shouted, "You're not Lao Jiu! How can the tone of your voice have changed so much? You don't have any of the accent of our hometown! You're not Lao Jiu! You definitely aren't Lao Jiu!"

"What? The tone of my voice? Yes, my tone of voice has changed, that's because the friends I hang out with now are all from other places."

"No! No! You're definitely not Lao Jiu! Lao Jiu wouldn't call them 'flowers,' he would call them 'bean curd meat.'"

"Yes, I'll talk to you in detail in the car! You'll understand in just five minutes."

They got into the car. Vroom! It drove off. In the quiet sound of the rain and the turning wheels of the car, the young man in the raincoat turned on the electric light with his finger and showed Lao Hui this note:

"Lao Hui: I was just about to say 'You, you're not dead yet!' but as soon as your cigarette lit up, I immediately recognized that you were the person I wanted to kill. The person I wanted to find was just like you. However, as soon as you said we were 'a pair!' I didn't dare to do it myself, so I called this brother to come. However, you may immediately not be okay. Please forgive me, I believe, we are still 'a pair!' Lao Jiu."

Two Female Types (Middle)

— Qi Wuwen

When the car started, it was drizzling, but the rain gradually increased, and the carriage was full of coolness. The conversational skills of the passengers seemed to have gradually dulled, and some had already leaned against their chairs to doze off. This female companion also closed her eyes pretending to sleep, but when the car stopped at the intermediate station, she always opened her eyes and asked me what place it was.

The car finally passed the new station. Most of the passengers were busy packing their luggage and putting on thicker clothes. This female companion also put on her raincoat again and added a scarf. I was still sitting still.

"Put on a piece of clothing! It's very cold outside," she kindly said to me.

"It's okay," I said.

"Put on a piece of clothing." This time she seemed to be ordering me.

"I don't feel cold." I didn't say that I didn't bring any thick clothes, I only thanked her for her kindness in my heart.

After getting off the car, I met the friend who came to pick me up. The three of us left the station together. I glanced at the partner sent by the ×× Hotel to pick up the car. I pointed it out to her, said goodbye, and followed my friend into the car that picked up guests from another hotel.

I've been to Tianjin no less than ten times, but I've never stayed there for more than three days. The first time I stayed in Tianjin for two days, I was sick for two days. I don't like Tianjin, which may be one reason. Speaking of Tianjin, it's not bad. The neat and clean streets and buildings, the modern equipment are like other big cities, and it's not as chaotic and noisy as Shanghai. However, precisely because of this, this northern metropolis is too ordinary. It lacks stimulation and appeal for tourists.

The reason I came to Tianjin this time was to see a classmate I hadn't seen for a long time. Another friend said that this friend was too "foreign" to the core. As soon as the car stopped, I saw him standing on the platform. His attire had added a bit of a gentlemanly air: he was wearing a coat with a swan collar, a cane was hanging on his arm, and he was holding a pair of gloves in his left hand.

When we arrived at the hotel, after talking about the situation since we had parted, he told me with a smile. .

"Josephine sent a letter recently, saying that she is engaged and will be married soon."

Josephine was his lover in France. They originally had an "engagement agreement", but after he returned to China, he knew that it was impossible to bring her to China, and he was currently weaving a Chinese lady. However, Josephine treated him too well, and as long as Josephine still loved him, he always felt a little burdened in his soul.

"Your burden can be lifted," I said.

"What kind of gift should I give her?" He smiled and then asked. His thoughtful gentlemanly manner towards women was revealed again.

He originally knew two women in Tianjin at the same time: one was a seventeen- or eighteen-year-old female student, and the other was a lady from a noble family. When he was hesitating between "bear's paw and fish", he also wrote to me asking me to make a decision for him. I returned him a letter of "refusal." Later, when he decided to take the lady from the noble family as his target of pursuit, I poured a bucket of cold water on him, but he was not angry.

"How are you doing with Miss Zhang?"

"There is no big problem," he replied triumphantly, "Miss Zhang is very understanding of me. The problem is her father, he wants me to find a job before he agrees to our engagement. Do you want to meet her?" (To be continued)

University Days (31)

— By the German Storm, translated by Chen Yinzhi

After a while, I stood up and walked into the hall. This hall was darker than I had imagined; the trees near the windows seemed to have branches growing to the roof. I tapped on the table with my cane, causing echoes in the tall ceiling; but no one came.—In a small room on the left I saw a lonely billiard table standing. But there was another door at the bottom of the hall on the other side; I opened the door, walked into a narrow passage, and through this passage I came to an open space again.—Near the house, next to a sports field, I found a middle-aged man with a green apron around his waist sleeping on the grass. In fact, this was the servant Ou!—When I touched him with my cane, he opened his eyes and jumped up. "I'm sorry, sir!" he said, "I was very busy last night and didn't sleep well."

I looked at him in surprise.

"Don't you know?" he continued, looking at me, from head to toe. "The university gentlemen have moved their club here since Easter."

I really didn't know, although most of my friends had joined this club.

I ordered a bottle of beer and a piece of bread, and we went back into the hall.—When the sunlight shone in through the open door, I saw many black spots in the center of the floor, and then I knew without a doubt: not only the club, but the fencing field attached to the club, had also moved to this quiet place.—"Why don't you wipe off these blood stains?" I asked.

"Please forgive me, sir!" replied the pale-faced servant Ou, "But the blood stains reappear after they are wiped off. This is what was left behind by that unfortunate incident.—When that enthusiastic young gentleman died so quietly and so pale, the situation was very tragic."

I immediately remembered the incident, where the widow left behind by a poor officer lost her only son in this incident. This happened not long after I returned home, and the incident aroused the sympathy of all the people in this small place.

I walked out of the hall and sat on a green bench, thinking about this poor, passionate young man; his life left a final unpleasant mark here.

After a while, the servant Ou brought me the breakfast I had ordered. "Tonight, you'll have good things to see," he said, putting the cups and plates on the table in front of me; "We have a dance party here, the boss has to send all the cooks from his house here."

"American-Style Pure Objectivism"

— Wang Jicong

Among many literary researchers, there are so-called "American-style pure objectivists". These gentlemen can not only write articles on literary theory and literary history, but also write large books studying literature, but when they write articles or books, they only "objectively" list the names of many writers, their works and their birth and death dates, and only "objectively" list the opinions of many famous literary researchers in history, without adding their own explanations or judgments. For example, when they are writing a book called "Introduction to Literature", they list the opinions of Juyou, Taine, Wilde, Tolstoy, Plekhanov, etc. in each chapter and section, without making any judgments about right and wrong, good and bad, leaving everything to "objective evaluation". Therefore, when you read such an "objective" "Introduction to Literature", you only see it written line by line: "Taine said…; Tolstoy said…", as for what literature is and how many problems in literature can be solved, no clear answers can be found in such works.

Such a literary theory work without judgment seems to be very "objective" on the surface. But in fact, it still contains the author's most important "subjective" views. The "American-style pure objectivist"'s consistent attitude of writing articles and compiling books in a "purely objective" manner is a manifestation of his consistent "subjective" views; moreover, in his "purely objective" narrative, he often intentionally or unintentionally expresses his "subjective dogmatism". For example, Hisama Kumawo's "A Theory of European Modern Literary Trends", which specializes in listing people's names and book titles, and his "Introduction to Literature", which piles up the opinions of various schools, are said to be very "objective" works, but on closer inspection, the author's humanistic "subjective" views still play a dominant role in Hisama Kumawo's two books.

Because of this, there are many conflicting opinions in such literary works. (For example, Taine and Wilde, Tolstoy and Plekhanov, their respective literary opinions are conflicting.) Now, the "American-style pure objectivist" piles up these conflicting opinions together without judgment to form a book. This not only shows their lack of the ability to distinguish right from wrong, but also results in the mixing of truth and falsehood, confusing the eyes of ordinary readers, so that they cannot recognize right and wrong. If such a "purely objective" book-writing method has been "subjectively" approved by the author, then the result is that truth and falsehood coexist, and right and wrong cannot be distinguished. Here we can't help but exclaim: the so-called "American-style pure objectivism" is really "yellow silk, young woman, grandson carrying mortar" (exquisite words)! We can only dare not praise it!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Mussolini's Dilemma: Victory and Defeat Are Both Difficult

— Fei

The Italian-Abyssinian (Ethiopian) issue has now entered a critical stage. With both sides taking extreme positions and mediation by Britain, France, and other countries proving ineffective, there are rumors of a major war breaking out within a week. The seriousness of the situation cannot be overstated.

Among the mediators, Britain is the most active. This is because Britain possesses a rich colony in Africa, and other countries also have considerable interests in Abyssinia. In the event that Italy conquers Abyssinia, a conflict of interest would be unavoidable. If Italy fails, there is also the danger of unrest in British territories. Therefore, Britain is the most vehemently opposed to the Italian-Abyssinian War.

Previously, the British cabinet met to discuss the Italian-Abyssinian issue. It is said that they have decided to adopt a policy of complete harmony with the League of Nations Covenant. The British government will likely instruct Sir Drummond, the British ambassador to Italy, to explain two points to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini: (1) If Italy wins, the suppressed anger of people of color will worsen the situation. (2) If Italy fails, the victory of black people over white people will cause open rebellion among the nationalities of various colonies. Therefore, regardless of the outcome, Britain is deeply worried.

This explanation by Britain has been direct and honest, truly reflecting the real situation. However, this statement is made from the perspective of Britain. Hypothetically, from Italy's perspective, assuming Italy wins, the other countries will be jealous due to conflicts of interest. In the event that Italy fails, the defeat of white people by black people would be intolerable.

However, Mussolini has now reached a point of no return. Having already unfurled the sails and mustered the courage, how can he retract now? Furthermore, Mussolini has three main objectives in this campaign against Abyssinia: (1) Italy suffered a loss of face in Abyssinia in the past, and now seeks to restore its honor. (2) Mussolini has trained hundreds of thousands of troops in recent years, and this provides an opportunity to showcase their strength. (3) After the European War, Italy did not receive the benefits of German territories, and this provides an opportunity to settle old scores.

However, considering the outcome of Italy's campaign against Abyssinia, victory and defeat are both difficult. Failure would not only wipe away a lifetime of reputation, but also lead to incalculable losses for Italy and changes in the international landscape. Even with victory, the aftermath may be even more complicated.

Pure Pleasures in the Dust #2

— Tan Tan

Many people think that living in the city means being deprived of any sense of pure pleasure. In fact, this is incorrect. In the previous article, I briefly wrote about some pure pleasures of living at home in the city. Now I would like to write about some pure pleasures outside of the home in the city.

Skyscrapers have become the symbol and backbone of modern cities. Many people, upon seeing these concrete and steel structures, deeply despise the "scholar hermits" of Lin Yutang and his ilk. In fact, they completely fail to understand what constitutes true interest.

Let's not even discuss the forms and lines of those skyscrapers, or their value in modern aesthetics. Simply imagine climbing to the very top at sunset and watching the clamorous disturbances of the city below, merging into a blurred scene, with countless wisps of cooking smoke weaving a misty twilight. The setting sun, obscured by smoke, is no longer blinding but allows one to see its complete, rounded form as it slowly sinks between several other skyscrapers. At this moment, as you look around at the vastness, a myriad of emotions rise within you: "Before me, I see no ancient sages; behind me, no successors appear. I think of the immensity of Heaven and Earth, and I weep, alone and overwhelmed."

Just as you are lost in deep thought, the colorful neon lights of the street awaken you, immediately drawing you into another realm. I don't know where the hazy and faint light of twilight has gone. What appears before you now is brightness and warmth, beauty and purity. Looking down, the cars on the street flow past like a river. The Later Lord Li's words, "Carriages flow like water, horses like dragons," become a reality. If it's the time of the full moon, because you are standing so high, no matter how bright the city lights may be, you can always see the moon by looking up. If your eyesight is good, you may even catch a glimpse of a few graceful stars twinkling at you. At this moment, your previous feeling of vast sorrow will surely deepen: "I want to ride the wind and fly home, yet I fear the jade towers and jeweled mansions are too cold up high." A gust of wind brings a slight chill, and you awaken as from a dream, realizing how high you are standing.

Of course, if you are strong, you can endure for a while longer; if you are weak, you cannot stay for even a moment.

Walking down from the skyscraper, it's already late at night. At that time, do not walk down the main street. Instead, find a few deserted streets to stroll along. It is best if you can find a street that is not paved with bright asphalt, and allow a gust of wind to stir up the dust and sand on the road, blowing it into your face as you look up. Stagger along, walking in solitude. The shops on the deserted street are already closed, except for the small pubs that stay open all night. If you have a few coins in your pocket, you might as well go up and have a few sips. The seat should naturally be by the window, and there need not be many people. Sip slowly, one mouthful at a time, and look out the window. The dim streetlights shine weakly. If heaven smiles and a light rain suddenly falls, that would be even more wonderful. As Lu You wrote in his poem, "Sparse lamps, a light rain, and maple trees by the pub." Only those who truly understand taste can appreciate this sorrowful interest.

Naturally, by this time, your sorrow has become like a fine wine aged for several years—faint yet potent. If that is still not enough, you might as well sit for a while longer. In less than an hour, a blind person, led by a child, will surely pass by beneath the pub, playing a desolate sanxian lute. At that moment, no matter how strong you are, you will certainly be defeated by sorrow. So you give some money, come down from the pub, and stroll home, pouring yourself a cup of strong tea until dawn, as you certainly won't be able to sleep tonight.

What I have described above is the true taste of the city. Although this taste is indeed sorrowful, its aftertaste will never bore you or make you shallow, unlike the pleasures of a decadent and materialistic life.

Travel Notes

— Si Quan

The morning after I received the news of my uncle's serious illness, the sky was fluttering with light rain. In my experience, the weather seems to be predetermined, and there is never a sunny day. In the cramped room, I turned on the light and had my breakfast. A watch seemed to be suffering from indigestion. After more than ten years of being together, it deliberately neglected its responsibility today; it couldn't run at four o'clock. But it certainly isn't that early now. I opened the small square window. The gloomy sky looked like a mourning face. My sharp observation couldn't tell what time it was. I had never gone to the station so early to wait for the train. Today I have to start that new experience. When I got on the streetcar, I thought about the annoying policeman who could comfortably inspect my luggage today. My uncle was sick, and I had visited the countryside three times, and each time I was disturbed by that annoying guy and almost got off the train. When that boring thought came to my mind, I deliberately messed up the luggage that I had organized in the car, and it was simply impossible to tell a shirt from a pair of socks. At the same time, I was sizing up that pair of rats who couldn't get any oil or water, using their sharp noses to try to find something they needed. That situation was quite enough to pass the time. When they put that pile of messy things back into the luggage, their faces must have turned red, like a ripe watermelon, or maybe they would scold "bastard" - that sound must not be as startling as being summoned to the manager's office for doing something wrong, they must lower their voice so low that I might not be able to hear it, just like a dumb person eating chili peppers.

The car stopped in front of the station gate. I first glanced at the platform from the car shed, and that annoying guy was indeed one of the three. But he looked even more energetic today, and the bulky body was covered with a raincoat, as if he were an important person seen in the newspaper. He was using his sharp eyes, like a searchlight, to shine from this side to that side. When I paid the fare, he lingered and was a leader. The horseshoe nails on the heels of his leather shoes rolled down the stone steps like hitting the keys of a piano, and in the

Page 18

In the humid air, the sound was so loud that I didn't dare let my dry eyelids, which hadn't slept all night, droop down listlessly again. At the same time, I took a deep breath into my lungs and straightened my chest, trying to look a little braver. But when I stood next to him, I was almost a head shorter than him. He opened my luggage on the stone steps as if he were picking up a chick. I looked at the wind so that the ruthless rain would not blow over and wet my luggage, and took out a cigarette from my pocket and lit it. At that time, I also thought about giving him one as a reward for taking care of my luggage for the fourth time, but I didn't have the courage, and I was afraid that he would suspect that my cigarette was mixed with narcotics, which would be difficult to explain.

The clock tower at the station struck eight, and there were eight minutes left before the train left, so I thought of the sick watch, and with the air of a doctor, I asked it to run for four hours, and then I put it to my ear to listen to it start working before I felt relieved. I was watching the clock tower, as if I were a lover waiting for an appointment, hoping that these eight minutes would pass quickly. I really felt too embarrassed by the many porters' eyes on me.

In the last two minutes, the passengers getting on the train crowded in. They jumped to avoid the raindrops falling from above, and were afraid that they would not be able to buy tickets in the two minutes. Everyone seemed so panicked. The guy had just given up on my luggage and wanted to search for a reliable person to make up for his wasted efforts. But I was also preparing to get on the train. In two minutes, it was enough time for me to buy a ticket, get on the train and find a seat, and I had to catch my trip.

Mr. Huang Suhe's Talented Student

— Zhang Wenyi's Work (Only Fourteen Years Old)

Walking in the Rain

— Yafei

With a bewildered heart, I stepped wearily onto the streets at dawn. The morning breeze gently brushed against me, while the drizzle fell softly in the sky. The streets were as quiet as death!

At the pier, I stood proudly among many children, looking at the suitcase lying quietly beside me, feeling a little lost in my heart:

—Children, my sudden departure this time can be said to be an accident; but I will be back soon!

At this time, there was no hypocrisy, no disgust around me, only innocent eyes and innocent laughter; but I would be separated from these little angels immediately after this moment. I felt a little lost, I felt a little sad! However, when I thought about going to pursue my own glorious future, an idea of excitement came to my mind.

—Mr., when will you come back? We will be looking forward to your return every night!

Ying'er's words struck my heart like an alarm bell, making me hesitate to answer.

—Ah! You wait! Probably not in the season when lychee flowers bloom.

I endured the hot tears and reluctantly replied with such a sentence. But will I really come back when the lychee flowers bloom? If I can't come back by then, how will they look forward to it! If they hope that I won't come back, how will they be disappointed! Ah! I deceived these innocent children.

—It's still more than half a year before the lychee flowers bloom; the days are so long! Mr., can't you come back sooner?

Ming'er was about to cry: He held the corner of my clothes with his small hands, as if afraid that I would spread my wings and fly away. I stroked his soft hair with my hand, lowered my head, and gently kissed him on the forehead, kissing him.

—Mr., when you come back, you must bring more good stories.

Xiao Qian was still jumping in front of me so lively, asking me to bring some stories; I nodded to her absently.

I really wanted to cry at this time, but I didn't dare to cry in front of this group of children; seeing more than a dozen pairs of small eyes staring at my face, I no longer had the courage to look at them; I was ashamed, I was in pain, I had many words to tell them, but every time I just spit it out to my mouth, it slipped back. I was silent, and they were silent. Between us, only the boundless silence reigned.

The drizzle was still falling endlessly. Many workers on the wharf were busy carrying goods and luggage. The passengers who came to take the boat also slowly crowded up. I looked at the watch on my wrist and knew that the time for departure was not far away; so I reluctantly comforted them and said:

—Come back, I must come back: At least I have to come back to see you often. Now it's raining heavily, you should go home quickly!

But they didn't leave, they still surrounded me foolishly, and in each pair of small eyes, they were full of enthusiastic and sincere tears.

The whistle roared three times, and I subconsciously picked up the suitcase and fled into the cabin like a fugitive, and fell on my bunk and cried. At this time, I cried as much as I wanted, cried freely, and released all the depression that had been accumulating for more than an hour, and I didn't care about the surprised stewards and passengers on the ship. I didn't even think about whether this group of children had gone back?

The whistle sounded again, and the ship moved slowly. I woke up from the bunk, wiped away my tears, and looked out from the round window, and saw that this group of innocent children were still standing foolishly on the pier, looking at the ship, so I ran to the deck in one breath, stood by the railing, took out a handkerchief from my pocket, and waved it to them, waving it, they also raised a small arm each and waved it to me, I waved the handkerchief to them, but a pile of unnatural wry smiles floated on my face!

The speed of the ship increased, and the shadows of this group of people quickly disappeared in my eyes. Before long, even the roof peaks of the pier could not be seen.

I staggered down the escalator step by step, walked back to the cabin, lay on my own bunk, and felt very tired. I wanted to rest quietly; but curled up in the corner of the bunk, as soon as I closed my eyes, those dozen pairs of small eyes and dozen small faces flashed clearly in front of me—sometimes it seemed like I was teaching them gymnastics in the garden, and sometimes it seemed like I was teaching them in the classroom. I couldn't sleep, I didn't want to sleep, I jumped up from the bunk irritably, but I fell down again without realizing a dizziness. I buried my head in the quilt, trying to calm my nerves, but I felt the ship shaking very badly. I sat up, pushed open the window and looked outside, and realized that the ship was already sailing on the sea.

The rain seemed denser than in the morning, and the sea surface seemed to be covered with a thick fog. The surroundings were blurred, and no trace of smoke waves could be seen in the distance. Only the sound of rain was noisy on the ship, and the roaring sound of the waves was composed into a symphony of the sea.
